Nikah — Marriage
advanced
15 min
Guarantee of Mahr by Father or Guardian
Discusses rulings on guarantee of mahr by father, guardian, and agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal effects of a father's guarantee of mahr for his minor daughter from a guardian's guarantee for a major woman, and apply the conditions for validity.

Core Idea
A father's guarantee of mahr for his minor daughter does not make him owner; she must consent after majority.

Guarantee of mahr (daman al-mahr) is a common scenario in marriage contracts. This lesson examines the nuanced rulings when the guarantor is the father or guardian of the bride. The key distinction lies in whether the woman is a major or minor, and whether the guarantor acts as an intermediary or a principal. We will explore the conditions for a valid guarantee, the rights of recourse, and the differing views of the Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of guarantor and the woman's status
First, determine whether the guarantor is the father (for a minor) or another guardian (for a major). Then note the woman's age and mental capacity.
The father of a minor acts as a safir (intermediary), not as an owner.
2
Analyze the legal effect of the guarantee on the guarantor's rights
For a major woman, the guardian is like a stranger; she can demand from either the guarantor or the husband. For a minor, the father does not own the mahr; he merely holds it.
The father's possession is by virtue of fatherhood, not as a contractor.
3
Apply the conditions for validity
Ensure that the husband is an adult, and that the guarantee is accepted in the session. Also note that a guarantee during terminal illness is invalid.
The acceptance must be explicit or by a representative in the same session.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf differs on the validity of the father discharging the price from the sale of the minor's property. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The father's discharge is valid but he is liable to the child for transgression.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad (in one narration) hold that accepting the mahr for a minor with no wealth implies the father's guarantee. The Hanafi response distinguishes between acceptance and guarantee.
The dispute is over the implication of acceptance, not the ruling itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البزازية: إذا أعطى الأب أرضاً في مهر امرأته ثم مات الأب قبل قبض المرأة لا تكون الأرض لها لأنها هبة من الأب لم تتم بالتسليم. فإن ضمن المهر وأدى الأرض عنه ثم مات قبل التسليم كانت الأرض للمرأة بيع فلا يبطل بالموت. وأما ضمان ولي المرأة المهر عن زوجها فلا يخلو: إما أن تكون كبيرة أو صغيرة. فإن كانت كبيرة فظاهر لأنه كالأجنبي إذا ضمن لها المهر ويثبت لها الخيار: إن شاءت طالبته وإن شاءت طالبت زوجها إن كان كبيراً وهي أهل للمطالبة. ويرجع الولي بعد الأداء على الزوج إن ضمن بأمره، سواء كانت الكبيرة عاقلة أو مجنونة. وأما إذا كانت صغيرة زوجها الأب وضمن مهرها فحقوقه لا ترجع إليه وإنما ملك لأنه سفير ومعبر. قبض مهر الصغيرة بحكم الأبوة لا باعتبار أنه عاقد، ولهذا لا يملكه بعد بلوغها إلا برضاها صريحاً أو دلالة بأن تسكت وهي بكر. بخلاف ما إذا باع مال الصغير وضمن الثمن عن المشتري فإنه لا يصح لأنه أصيل فيه حتى ترجع الحقوق عليه ويصح إبراؤه من الثمن عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. لكنه يضمنه للولد لتعديه بالإبراء ويملك قبض الثمن بعد بلوغه، والضمان لصار ضامناً لنفسه. وبهذا علم أن قوله: «وتطالب زوجها أو وليها» مخصوص بما إذا كان الضامن وليها مع أن الحكم أعم. فلو قال: وتطالب زوجها أو الولي الضامن لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الضامن وليه. وقول الشارح الزيلعي في الصورة الثانية: «فالمطالبة إلى ولي الزوج مكان وليها» غير صحيح؛ المطالبة عليه لا إليه، وجعل «إلى» بمعنى «على» هنا مجاز بعيد. ولا بد من تقييد الزوج بالبلوغ لأنه ليس لها مطالبة الصغير بل وليها فقط. ولا بد من تقييد صحة ضمانه لها من قبولها أو قبول قابل في المجلس لأن الموجد شطر فلا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس في المذهب كما في البزازية. وظاهره أنه لا فرق بين الصغيرة والكبيرة. وإطلاقهم صحة ضمان مهر الصغيرة يقتضي أن لا يشترط قبول أحد في المجلس وأن إيجابه يكون مقام القبول عنها. ولا بد من التقييد بصحة وليها إذ ضمانه في مرضه باطل لما قدمنا من أن الضمان في مرض مالك على الأب، والشافعي وأحمد في رواية وافقاه. لأن قبول المهر عن صغير لا مال له دليل على ضمانه. قلنا: لا دلالة لقبوله المهر عنه بل على أدائه من مال الصغير قبل البلوغ إذا حصل مال له أو على أداء ابنه بنفسه بعد بلوغه. وأشار بصحة ضمان الولي إلى صحة ضمان الرسول في النكاح والوكيل بالأولى. فلو ضمن الرسول المهر ثم جحد الزوج الرسالة اختلف المشايخ فيما يلزم الرسول. وصح في المحيط أن المرأة إذا طلبت التفريق من القاضي وفرق بينها وبين الزوج كان لها على الرسول نصف المهر، وإن لم تطلب التفريق كان لها جميع المهر. ولو زوجه الوكيل على ألف من ماله أو على هذه الألف لم يلزمه شيء، ولو ضمن المهر لزمه، فإن كان بغير إذن الزوج فلا رجوع له. بخلاف الوكيل بالخلع فإنه إذا ضمن البدل عنها رجع به عليها، وإن لم تأمره بالضمان لانصراف التوكيل إلى الأمر بالضمان لصحة الخلع بلا توكيل منها. بخلاف النكاح فإنه لا يصح بلا توكيل منها فانصرف الأمر إليه. ولو زوجه الوكيل امرأة على عرضه جاز، فإن هلك في يد الوكيل رجعت بقيمته على الزوج، وفي الخلع ترجع على الوكيل. والكل من المحيط.
And in Al-Bazzaziyyah: If a father gives land as mahr for his wife then dies before the woman takes possession, the land does not belong to her because it is a gift from the father not completed by delivery. But if he guarantees the mahr and pays the land for it then dies before delivery, the land becomes the woman's as a sale and is not invalidated by death. As for the guardian of a woman guaranteeing the mahr from her husband, it depends: if she is a major, then it is apparent because he is like a stranger if he guarantees her mahr, and she has the option: if she wishes she may demand from him, and if she wishes she may demand from her husband if he is an adult and she is eligible to demand. The guardian after payment has recourse against the husband if he guaranteed by his order, whether the major woman is sane or insane. As for if she is a minor married by her father and he guaranteed her mahr, then rights do not revert to him and he possesses only as an intermediary and agent. He receives the mahr of the minor by virtue of fatherhood, not as a contractor, hence he does not own it after her majority except with her explicit consent or implicitly by her staying silent while she is a virgin. Unlike if he sells the property of a minor and guarantees the price from the buyer, this is not valid because he is principal so rights revert to him, and his discharge of the price is valid according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf. But he guarantees it to the child due to his transgression by discharge, and he owns receipt of the price after his majority, and the guarantee becomes a guarantee for himself. From this it is known that his saying: 'And she may demand her husband or her guardian' is specific to when the guarantor is her guardian, whereas the ruling is general. So if he said: 'And she may demand her husband or the guaranteeing guardian' it would be better to include when the guarantor is her guardian. And the statement of the commentator al-Zayla'i in the second scenario: 'The demand is to the guardian of the husband instead of her guardian' is incorrect; the demand is upon him, not to him, and making 'to' mean 'upon' here is a far-fetched metaphor. It is necessary to restrict the husband to maturity because she cannot demand from a minor, only her guardian can. And it is necessary to restrict the validity of his guarantee for her to her acceptance or the acceptance of a representative in the session because what exists is a part, and it does not depend on what is beyond the session in the madhhab as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between minor and major. Their absolute statement of the validity of guaranteeing the mahr of a minor implies that no one's acceptance is required in the session and that his offer takes the place of acceptance for her. It is necessary to restrict it to the validity of her guardian, for his guarantee in his terminal illness is invalid because, as we have stated, the guarantee in illness is property of the father, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration agreed with him, because accepting the mahr for a minor who has no wealth is evidence of his guarantee. We say: There is no evidence in his acceptance of the mahr for him; rather it indicates payment from the minor's wealth before puberty if he acquires wealth, or that his son pays it himself after puberty. And he indicated by the validity of the guardian's guarantee the validity of the guarantee of the messenger in marriage and the agent a fortiori. If the messenger guarantees the mahr then the husband denies the message, the scholars differed on what is incumbent on the messenger. And it is established in al-Muhit that if the woman requests separation from the judge and he separates between her and the husband, half the mahr is due from the messenger, and if she does not request separation, the entire mahr is due from him. And if the agent married him for a thousand from his wealth or for this thousand, nothing is incumbent on him, but if he guaranteed the mahr, it becomes incumbent. If it was without the husband's permission, he has no recourse. Contrary to the agent for khul', for if he guarantees the substitute for her, he has recourse against her, even if she did not order him to guarantee, because the agency implies the order to guarantee for the validity of khul' without her agency. Unlike marriage, it is not valid without her agency, so the order (to guarantee) is not implied. And if the agent married a woman for his own 'ard (commodity), it is valid. If it perishes in the agent's hand, she has recourse for its value against the husband, and in khul' she has recourse against the agent. All from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings on guarantee of mahr by a father or guardian. It opens with a ruling from Al-Bazzaziyyah about a father giving land as mahr. If the father dies before the woman takes possession, the land does not go to her because it was a gift not completed. But if the father guaranteed the mahr and paid the land as substitute, then it is a sale and the woman gets the land even after father's death. 

Then it discusses the guardian's guarantee. If the woman is major, the guardian is like any stranger; she can demand from the guarantor or the husband. The guarantor can recover from the husband if he guaranteed by his order. If the woman is minor and married by her father, the father's guarantee is different: he receives the mahr as guardian, not as contractor. After she reaches majority, she only gets the mahr if she consents explicitly or implicitly (by silence as a virgin). This differs from selling a child's property where the father is principal. 

The text then clarifies a phrase from the matn: 'And she may demand her husband or her guardian' applies only when the guarantor is her guardian. It criticizes al-Zayla'i's wording. It also notes necessary restrictions: the husband must be adult, acceptance must be in the session for the guarantee to be valid. The guarantee in illness is invalid because it is like a will. 

Finally, it extends the ruling to a messenger or agent who guarantees the mahr: if the husband denies the agency, the messenger's liability depends on whether separation occurs. The agent's liability differs from the agent for khul'. All these details are from Al-Muhit.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): A guardian who has authority over a woman's marriage, such as the father or grandfather.
ضمان (daman): A guarantee by which a person becomes responsible for a debt or obligation of another.
مهر (mahr): The dower that a husband must give to his wife upon marriage, either specified or the mahr al-mithl.
سفير (safir): An intermediary who acts on behalf of another without being a party to the contract.
معبر (mu'abbar): One who expresses or conveys, similar to safir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father guarantees the mahr for his minor daughter's marriage and receives it, what happens to the mahr after she reaches majority?
A) The father keeps the mahr for himself as compensation for his guarantee.
B) The daughter automatically owns the mahr without any requirement.
C) The daughter does not own it unless she consents, either explicitly or by remaining silent while being a virgin.
D) The mahr is considered a loan from the father and must be repaid.

Key Takeaway
The legal capacity of the guarantor and the woman's status determine the rights and obligations in mahr guarantee; a father's guarantee for a minor daughter does not give him ownership, and explicit guarantee is required for liability.

Wife's Right to Withhold Until Mahr is Paid
Discusses a woman's right to prevent intercourse and travel until she receives her mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's right to withhold from intercourse and travel until her mahr is paid, and explain the qiyas argument that supports it, including the response to the objection regarding specific mahr items.

Core Idea
Even after intercourse, a wife may withhold from her husband until she actually receives her mahr.

This lesson examines a pivotal Hanafi ruling in marriage contracts: the wife's right to prevent intimacy and travel until her mahr is delivered. The ruling rests on a qiyas (analogy) to sale, which this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq carefully defends against objections from later scholars. Understanding this ruling clarifies the mahr's role as a rightful compensation that must be physically received.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the wife's right: she may prevent her husband from intercourse and from taking her out of her town until the full mahr is paid. Note that this right persists even after she has had intercourse.
The right is not lost by consummation.
2
Understand the qiyas to sale
The basis is that once the wife delivers herself, her right to the mahr (badal) becomes determined like the husband's right to marital benefit (mubaddal). This is analogous to a sale where each party can withhold delivery until the other delivers.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear analogy) because the exchange relationship is similar.
3
Examine the objection from Fath al-Qadir
The objection states that this qiyas only works when the mahr is a debt. For a specific item (e.g., a slave), the wife owns it by contract, so her right is already determined and she cannot withhold after intercourse.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response clarifies that 'delivery' here means takhliya (clearing obstacles). Even for a specific item, physical delivery is needed to remove it from the husband's guarantee (daman). Until then, the item remains his risk, so she may withhold.
The text uses the example of barter sale to show that simultaneous delivery is possible, but in marriage it is not.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the wife may withhold until actual delivery, whether the mahr is a debt or a specific item. This protects the wife's right to receive her mahr fully.
This is the position in Al-Hidayah and Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر وإن وطئها. أي للمرأة منع نفسها من وطء الزوج وإخراجها من بلدها حتى يوفيها مهرها إن كانت قد سلمت نفسها للوطء فوطئها لتعين حقها في البدل كما تعين حق الزوج في المبدل فصار كالبيع. كذا في الهداية. وأورد عليه في فتح القدير بأن هذا التحليل لا يصح إلا في الصداق الدين، أما العين كما لو تزوجها على عبد بعينه فلا لأنها بالعقد ملكته وتعين حقها فيه حتى ملكت عتقه. وقد قالوا في بيع المقايضة: يقال لهما سلما معاً، ويمكن أن يكون هنا كذلك فلها المنع قبله. وما في فتح القدير من أن مثله لا يتأتي في النكاح إذا كان المهر عبداً معيناً مثلاً ولا في معية الخلوة لإطلاق الجواب بأن لها الامتناع إلى أن تقبض. ففيه نظر، لأن المراد بالتسليم هنا التخلية برفع الموانع وهو ممكن في العبد أيضاً بأن يخلي بينها وبين بشروط التخلية. ثم أجاب عنه في النهر بأنه يمكن أن يقال: المراد التعيين التام المخرج عن الضمان ولن يكون ذلك إلا بالتسليم ألا ترى أن عبد المهر في ضمانه ما بقي في يده. وقد قالوا في بيع المقايضة الخ تمهيد لما بعده وهو قوله: وما في فتح القدير الخ لا جواب عما قبله. قال الرملي: يعني القول لهما سلما معاً. وقوله: ولا في معية الخلوة يعني لا يتأتي مثله في النكاح ولا في معية الخلوة أي أن يقال لهما سلما معاً فيهما أي لا يتأتي معية الخلوة وتسليم المهر معاً. الإطلاق الجواب الخ تعليل لقوله لا يتأتى أي لا يتأتى التسليم هنا كما في بيع المقايضة لقولهم لها...
And she may prevent him from intercourse and taking her out for the mahr, even if he had intercourse with her. That is, a woman may prevent herself from the husband's intercourse and from being taken out of her town until he pays her mahr, if she had delivered herself for intercourse and he had intercourse with her because her right in the substitute (badal) became determined just as the husband's right in the object (mubaddal) became determined, so it is like a sale. Thus in Al-Hidayah. And it was objected to in Fath al-Qadir that this analysis is valid only for a dower that is a debt; as for a specific item like if he married her on a specific slave, then it is not because she owned it by the contract and her right to it became determined so that she owned its manumission. And they said in barter sale: it is said that both gave delivery simultaneously, and it is possible that it is likewise here, so she may prevent before that. And what is in Fath al-Qadir that such a thing is not possible in marriage when the mahr is a specific slave for example, nor in the simultaneous occurrence of the seclusion and the delivery of the mahr because the answer was given absolutely that she may refuse until she receives. There is consideration in it, because what is meant by delivery here is clearing (takhliya) by removing obstacles, and that is also possible in the slave by clearing him for her with the conditions of clearing. Then it was answered in Al-Nahr that it can be said: what is meant is the complete specification that removes from the guarantee, and that only occurs by delivery. Do you not see that the slave of the mahr is in his guarantee as long as it remains in his hand. And they said in barter sale... [text incomplete]
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a woman's right to prevent her husband from having intercourse with her and from taking her out of her town until she receives her mahr, even after she has allowed intercourse. The basis is that once she has delivered herself and he has had intercourse, her right to the dower becomes specifically established (ta'ayyun) just as the husband's right to the marital benefit becomes specific. This is analogous to a sale where both parties have rights in the exchanged items. The ruling is from Al-Hidayah.

Then an objection from Fath al-Qadir is presented: this analogy only works when the mahr is a debt, not when it is a specific item like a slave. Because upon marriage, she owns the specific item immediately and her right is already determined. So she would not have the right to withhold after intercourse. The text responds by saying that even for a specific item, delivery (takhliya) is required to complete the right. Until then, the item remains in the husband's guarantee, so she may withhold. This is supported by the analogy of barter sale (بيع المقايضة) where both parties are considered to have delivered simultaneously. However, that simultaneous delivery is not possible in marriage because seclusion (khulwa) and delivery of the mahr cannot occur together. The final response from Al-Nahr clarifies that complete specification removing the item from guarantee only occurs with actual delivery. Thus, the woman's right to withhold remains until she physically receives the mahr, even if it is a specific item.

The relied-upon Hanafi position is that she may withhold until she receives the mahr, whether it is a debt or a specific item.

Key Terms
تعين (ta'ayyun): The specification or determination of a right to a specific thing, so that it is no longer subject to change.
تسليم (taslim): Delivery or handing over of the married item, but here interpreted as takhliya (clearing of obstacles).
تخلية (takhliya): Clearing the way for the woman to take possession, e.g., of a slave, by removing the husband's control.
بدل (badal): The substitute or compensation, here the mahr that the wife will receive.
مبدل (mubaddal): The thing given in exchange, here the marital benefit (al-bud') that the husband receives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a woman prevent her husband from intercourse even after she has had intercourse with him, if the mahr is a specific item?
A) Yes, she can prevent him until she receives the specific item.
B) No, because she already owns the specific item by the contract.
C) Only if the mahr is a debt; for a specific item she cannot because she owns it.
D) She can only prevent travel, not intercourse.

Key Takeaway
The wife retains the right to withhold from intercourse and travel until she physically receives the mahr, whether it is a debt or a specific item.

intermediate

Wife's Right to Withhold and Guarantee of Guardian and Messenger
Rulings on wife's withholding and third-party guarantees for mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wife's right to withhold herself for unpaid mahr and analyze the guarantee of the guardian and messenger in marriage.

Core Idea
The wife may withhold intercourse and travel until the mahr is paid, and a guardian's guarantee of the mahr is only valid if he is her heir.

Marriage establishes the wife's right to the mahr, which becomes a debt owed by the husband. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses her remedies: she may withhold herself from intercourse and travel until payment. It then examines the liability of a guardian who guarantees the mahr, and the distinct roles of messenger and agent. Understanding these rules clarifies the interaction between marriage contract obligations and third-party guarantees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's right and its trigger
The wife may prevent her husband from intercourse and from taking her out of the home until the mahr is paid. This right persists even after intercourse, because the mahr is a binding debt.
Contrast with a sale: once possession is taken, the seller cannot withhold; but here the right remains.
2
Analyze the effect of intercourse on her right
The text explicitly states she may prevent even if he has had intercourse. Her right is not extinguished by consummation; it remains until the mahr is fulfilled.
Some mistakenly think intercourse waives the right, but the Hanafi view preserves it.
3
Examine the guarantee of the guardian
A guardian's guarantee of the mahr is valid only if he is the woman's heir at the time of his death. If not (e.g., he is a paternal cousin with another heir), the guarantee is invalid and must come from the guardian's own wealth (from the third of his estate).
The validity depends on inheritance connection, not mere guardianship.
4
Distinguish the liability of messenger vs. agent
If the messenger guarantees the mahr and the husband denies the messengership, scholars differed. The relied-upon view: if the woman seeks separation, she gets half the mahr from the messenger; otherwise, the full mahr. An agent who guarantees the mahr is liable, but without the husband's permission he has no recourse. Contrast with khul' agents, who have recourse.
Messenger (rasul) has limited authority; agent (wakil) has broader discretion.

Source Text

ولها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر وإن وطئها وإن اختلفا في قدر المهر حكم مهر الموت للوارث أو عنه باطل، وينبغي تقييده بما إذا كانت موليته وارثته، وأما إذا لم تكن وارثته كما إذا كانت بنت عمه مثلاً وله وارث يحجبها فالضمان صحيح مطلقاً كما لا يخفى ويكون من الثلث كما قدمناه وأشار بصحة ضمان الولي إلى صحة ضمان الرسول في النكاح والوكيل بالأولى، فلو ضمن الرسول المهر ثم جحد الزوج الرسالة اختلف المشايخ فيما يلزم الرسول، وصح في المحيط أن المرأة، إذا طلبت التفريق من القاضي وفرق بينها وبين الزوج كان لها على الرسول نصف المهر، وإن لم تطلب التفريق كان لها جميع المهر. ولو زوجه الوكيل على ألف من ماله أو على هذه الألف لم يلزمه شيء، ولو ضمن المهر لزمه، فإن كان بغير إذن الزوج فلا رجوع له بخلاف الوكيل بالخلع فإنه إذا ضمن البدل عنها رجع به عليها، وإن لم تأمره بالضمان لانصراف التوكيل إلى الأمر بالضمان لصحة الخلع بلا توكيل منها بخلاف النكاح فإنه لا يصح بلا توكيل منها فانصرف الأمر إليه ولو زوجه الوكيل إمرأة على عرضه جاز، فإن هلك في يد الوكيل رجعت بقيمته على الزوج وفي الخلع ترجع على الوكيل، والكل من المحيط .
And she has the right to prevent him from intercourse and from taking her out for the mahr, even if he has had intercourse with her. And if they differ about the amount of the mahr, the mahr of the like is ruled, and the mahr of the deceased goes to the heir or from him is invalid. And it should be restricted to when his client is his heir. But if she is not his heir, like if she is his paternal cousin and he has an heir that prevents her, then the guarantee is valid absolutely, as is not hidden, and it is from the third as we have mentioned. And his indication of the validity of the guardian's guarantee indicates the validity of the guarantee of the messenger in marriage, and the agent a fortiori. So if the messenger guarantees the mahr then the husband denies the messengership, the scholars differed regarding what is required from the messenger. And it is established in al-Muhit that the woman, if she seeks separation from the judge and he separates between her and the husband, then she has half the mahr from the messenger, and if she does not seek separation, she has all the mahr. And if the agent marries him for a thousand from his own wealth or for this thousand, nothing is required from him. And if he guarantees the mahr, it is required from him. If it is without the husband's permission, he has no recourse, unlike the agent for khul' because if he guarantees the substitute for her, he has recourse against her, even if she did not command him to guarantee, because the agency extends to the command to guarantee due to the validity of khul' without her agency, unlike marriage because it is not valid without her agency, so the command extends to it. And if the agent marries a woman to him on his collateral, it is permissible. Then if it perishes in the hand of the agent, she returns by its value against the husband, and in khul' she returns against the agent. All from al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several rulings. First, it states the wife's right to prevent her husband from intercourse and from taking her out of her home or city until the mahr is paid. This right remains even if he has already had intercourse, because her right to the mahr has become established like a sale. The text then discusses the case of a guardian who guarantees the mahr: it is valid only if the guardian is the woman's heir; if not, it is invalid and comes from the guardian's own third of his wealth. The text also covers the messenger and agent in marriage. If the messenger guarantees the mahr and the husband denies the messengership, the scholars differ; the relied-upon view in al-Muhit is that if the woman seeks separation, she gets half the mahr from the messenger; if not, she gets the full mahr. Regarding the agent, if he marries on his own wealth, nothing is required; if he guarantees, it is binding. The agent has no recourse without permission, unlike the agent for khul' who does have recourse. Finally, if the agent marries on a collateral that perishes, the woman recovers its value from the husband, while in khul' she recovers from the agent.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift that the husband gives to the wife as an obligation of marriage.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the woman in marriage, usually her father or paternal relative.
الرسول (al-rasul): The messenger sent by the husband to contract the marriage on his behalf.
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent appointed to act on behalf of another in legal matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to withhold for mahr is a powerful remedy that survives consummation, and third-party guarantees are subject to conditions tied to inheritance and agency.

The Wife's Right to Withhold for Mahr and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary with objection and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the wife's right to withhold intercourse and travel until the mahr is paid, differentiate between Abu Hanifa's view and that of the Sahibayn regarding coercion, and defend the analogy to barter sale against the objection from Fath al-Qadir.

Core Idea
Even after consummation, a wife may withhold intercourse until her mahr is paid — like a barter sale where both must deliver simultaneously.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks a critical marital right: the wife's prerogative to withhold herself from intercourse and travel until her dower is delivered. The commentator clarifies that this right persists even after consummation and is grounded in the exchange nature of marriage, analogous to a barter sale. However, objections arise regarding specific mahr items and an intra-Hanafi split emerges on whether the husband may coerce if she withholds. We will navigate the objections and the dispute to arrive at the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling
Locate the core hakm: the wife may prevent intercourse and travel until the mahr is paid, even if consummation has occurred. Note that this is her right, not an obligation.
The matn phrase is 'ولها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر وإن وطئها'.
2
Understand the analogy to sale
The commentator compares marriage to a barter sale (bay' al-muqayaḍa) where both parties deliver consideration simultaneously. Just as in a sale, the wife's right to the mahr is established and she may withhold until she receives it.
The analogy relies on the idea of badal (substitute) and mubaddal (substituted).
3
Analyze the objection from Fath al-Qadir
An objection is raised: the analogy only works for a debt mahr, not a specific item (e.g., a slave). In the objection, the wife owns the specific item immediately upon contract, so she cannot withhold. The commentator responds by clarifying that 'delivery' here means removing obstacles, which is possible even for a specific item.
This is a key point: possession vs. ownership. Ownership may transfer at contract, but actual possession (taslim) may still be pending.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on coercion
The passage notes a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the husband may NOT coerce intercourse if she refuses for the mahr (la yahill). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that it IS permissible (yahill). Consider the thamarah alkhilaf: sinfulness vs. permissibility of coercion.
The text does not give a clear tarjih, but later authorities may prefer Abu Hanifa in matters of sexual ethics.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
The passage ends with a classification of thirteen scenarios based on whether the mahr is immediate, deferred, partially deferred, etc., and whether entry is conditioned. Practice identifying the ruling for each scenario.
This shows the practical application of the principle.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn phrase 'ولها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر وإن وطئها'. The commentator explains that the wife may prevent intercourse and travel until the mahr is paid, even if she had already been intimate, because her right to the mahr has been established like a sale. An objection from Fath al-Qadir is mentioned: this analogy only works for a debt mahr, not a specific item like a slave, because she owns it immediately at the contract. The commentator responds by citing the analogy to barter sale (bay' al-muqayaḍa) where both parties deliver simultaneously, and argues that here too she may prevent until she receives the mahr, even if it is a specific item. The discussion continues with references to al-Nahr and al-Bada'i', and a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether the husband may coerce intercourse if she refuses for the mahr: Abu Hanifa says it is not permissible, while the two companions say it is permissible. The author then indicates various rulings: the wife may go out for her needs, the father may travel with his virgin daughter before and after payment of the mahr, and the detail about when the mahr is immediate or deferred. The passage ends with a classification of thirteen scenarios based on the terms of the mahr.

Key Terms
الصداق (al-sadaq): Synonym for mahr, the dower.
بيع المقايضة (bay' al-muqayaḍa): A barter sale where both parties exchange goods simultaneously.
الخلوة (al-khalwa): Seclusion (between spouses) that establishes certain rights.

15 min
Wife's Right to Withhold Herself for Mahr
Detailed rulings on wife's right to withhold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wife may withhold herself from her husband due to non-payment of mahr, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling to various scenarios.

Core Idea
A wife may withhold herself only if the mahr is immediately due; deferral waives her right, though Abu Yusuf allows it by istihsan.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi ruling regarding a wife's right to refuse intercourse or cohabitation (imtina') until she receives her mahr. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the default rule based on analogy to sale, the key exception introduced by Abu Yusuf through istihsan, and numerous sub-cases involving deferred mahr, unknown terms, and the effect of divorce. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the type of mahr stipulation and the doctrinal tension between qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
The wife's right to withhold (imtina') is a legal consequence of the husband's obligation to pay mahr. Determine whether the mahr is immediately due (hal) or deferred (mu'ajjal).
2
State the default Hanafi ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, if the entire mahr is deferred, the wife has no right to withhold. If any part is immediate, she may withhold until she receives that part.
The ruling is based on qiyas to sale: a buyer cannot withhold payment after agreeing to a term.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues by istihsan that even with full deferral, the wife may withhold because the husband's request for deferral implies consent to delay consummation.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here due to custom and need.
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the wife must submit immediately; under Abu Yusuf, she may refuse until paid.
Fatwa differed: al-Walwaliji favored Abu Yusuf; later scholars differed.
5
Apply to sub-cases
The passage covers many sub-cases: partial deferral, unknown terms (approximate vs. excessive), stipulation of entry before receipt, hawala (transfer of debt), and effect of divorce.
Focus on the principle: custom is considered only if explicit stipulation is absent.

اشتراط الحلول أو تأجيل الكل أو حالاً قال الولوالجي : وبقول أبي يوسف يفتى استحساناً بخلاف البيع ا هـ. ولأن العادة جارية بتأخير الدخول عند تأخير جميع المهر. وفي الخلاصة أن الأستاذ ظهير الدين كان يفتي بأنه ليس له الامتناع والصدر الشهيد كان يفتي بأن لها ذلك ا هـ. فقد اختلفت الفتوى . وفي معراج الدراية : إذا كان المهر مؤجلاً ثم حل الأجل فليس لها الامتناع عند أبي حنيفة، ولم أر حكم ما إذا كان الأجل سنة مثلا فلم تسلم نفسها حتى مضى الأجل هل يصير أو لا بد من سنة بعد التسليم كما قال أبو حنيفة في البيع، فإن قيس النكاح على البيع صح لأنهم اعتبروه به هنا. وفي المحيط وغيره : لو أحالت المرأة رجلاً على زوجها بالمهر فلها الامتناع إلى أن يقبض المحتال لأن غريمها بمنزلة وكيلها ، وإن أحالها الزوج بمهرها ليس لها الامتناع، وهذا إذا كان الأجل معلوماً، فإن كان مجهولا ، فإن كانت جهالة متقاربة كالحصاد والدياس ونحو ذلك فهو كالمعلوم، وهذه على وجوه : إما أن يصرح بحلول كله أو تعجيله أو حلول بعضه وتأجيل بعضه أو تأجيل كله أجلاً معلوماً أو مجهولاً أو متقارباً أو متفاحشاً فهي سبعة، وكل منها إما بشرط الدخول قبل القبض أو لا. فهي أربعة عشر، وكل منها إما أن يكون المنع قبل التسليم أو بعده فهي ثمانية وعشرون على الصحيح كما في الظهيرية بخلاف البيع فإنه لا يجوز بهذا الشرط. وإن كانت متفاحشة كإلى الميسرة أو إلى هبوب الريح أو إلى أن تمطر السماء فالأجل لا يثبت ويجب المهر حالاً. كذا في غاية البيان. وظاهره أن التأجيل إلى الطلاق أو الموت متفاحش فيجب المال حالاً بمقتضى إطلاق العقد، والظاهر خلافه لجريان العرف بالتأجيل به وذكر في الخلاصة والبزازية اختلافاً فيه وصحح أنه وحكم التأجيل بعد العقد كحكمه فيه كما في فتح القدير أيضاً. وهذا كله إذا لم يشترط الدخول قبل حلول الأجل، فلو شرطه ورضيت ليس لها الامتناع اتفاقاً كما في الفتح أيضاً. وفي الخلاصة : وبالطلاق يتعجل المؤجل ولو راجعها لا يتأجل ا.هـ. يعني إذا كان التأجيل إلى الطلاق، أما إذا كان التأجيل إلى مدة معينة لا يتعجل بالطلاق كما يقع في ديار مصر في بعض الأنكحة أنهم يجعلون بعضها حالاً وبعضه مؤجلاً إلى الطلاق أو إلى الموت، وبعضه منجماً في كل سنة قدر معين، فإذا طلقها تعجل البعض المؤجل لا المنجم لأنها تأخذه بعد الطلاق على نجومه كما تأخذه قبل الطلاق على نجومه وذكر قولين في الفتاوى الصيرفية في صحيح . البعض إما أن يكون بعد العقد أو لا قوله : (ولا) اعتبار بالعرف إذا جاء الصريح بخلافه) يعني لها الامتناع حتى تستوفي الكل فيما لو شرطا الحلول وإن كان ثم عرف في تعجيل البعض وتأجيل البعض ولا يعتبر ذلك العرف للتصريح بخلافه قوله : (وفي معراج الدراية) قال الرملي : هذا اختيار لما أفتي به الأستاذ ظهير الدين ووجهه أنه لما وقع العقد موجباً لتسليمها قبل قبض المهر بالتأجيل لا يمتنع ذلك بحلول الأجل تأمل قوله : (ليس لها الامتناع اتفاقاً قال نوح أفندي: في كلام قاضيخان
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr. And she withholds herself by removing obstacles from her, and they are equal. This is before seeing the transmission. Then I saw in al-Muhit: If the mahr is a specific item, they both exchange/grasp as in barter sale. End quote. By this, what is in Fath al-Qadir falls. The author indicated by preventing him from what was mentioned that he does not prevent her from going out for her needs and visiting without his permission before receiving the mahr because she is not confined for his right, unlike after he pays it because she is confined for him. And that the father may travel with his virgin daughter even if she is adult before payment of mahr and after it no, not as in Fath al-Qadir. And that it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her against her will before payment. He said in al-Muhit on nafaqah: Is it permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her against her will? If the refusal is not for demanding mahr, it is permissible because she is unjust; if for demanding mahr, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible. End quote. And he gave absolute in 'ikharaj' (removal), so it includes removal from her house and from her city; he does not have that. And interpreting 'ikharaj' as traveling with her, as in al-Hidayah, is not appropriate, as it suggests he can remove her from her house to another house in her city. And he gave absolute in mahr, and there is detail. The summary: either they explicitly stipulate its immediacy or its deferral entirely, or immediacy of part and deferral of part, or they remain silent. If they stipulate its immediacy or its promptness entirely, she may withhold until she receives it all; immediacy and promptness are synonymous. Custom is not considered when explicit stipulation contradicts it. Similarly, if they stipulate immediacy of part, she may withhold until she receives the stipulated part only. As for deferral of the whole, she has no right to withhold at all, because she waived her right by deferral as in sale. And from Abu Yusuf that she has the right to withhold by istihsan, because when he requested deferral of the entire sum, he has consented to waive his right to enjoyment. Because the withholding is until she receives. His saying: By this, what is in Fath al-Qadir falls. He said in al-Nahr: What is in al-Fath is transmitted from their speech. He said in al-Bada'i: If the price is a specific item, they both deliver together, and here the delivery of mahr is advanced in all cases, whether it is a debt or a specific item, because simultaneous grasp and delivery are impossible, unlike in sale. End quote. In al-Muhit: The presence of the woman is not required for the father to receive the mahr of his daughter; according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar it is required. And for them, custom has it that the woman's delivery is delayed after receipt of her dower for some time; when the husband knows this, he consents to advancing the dower and delaying her delivery, not so in sale. End quote. This is only consistent with what is in al-Bada'i. So the first part in al-Muhit, i.e., what the author cited, is taken as a narration. His saying: (Even if she is adult) The phrase of al-Fath: For the father to travel with the virgin before payment. Similarly in al-Fatawa: He married off his adult virgin daughter, then wanted to move to another city with his family; he may take her with him even if the husband dislikes it. If he gave her the mahr, he may confine her. So the author took generality from the absolute wording of al-Fath, or understood that the restriction to adult in al-Fatawa is incidental. His saying: (After it, no) i.e., after the husband pays the mahr, the father may not travel with her. His saying: The summary is that either they explicitly stipulate) He did not mention all cases explicitly. So we say: Either they explicitly stipulate its immediacy or its deferral, or immediacy of some and deferral of some, or they are silent. In the last two, either the term is known or unknown, approximate or excessive. In each case, either they stipulate entry before the term expires or not. So there are thirteen cases. In stipulating immediacy or deferral of all or immediately. al-Walwaliji said: By Abu Yusuf's statement, fatwa is given by istihsan, unlike sale. End quote. Because custom is to delay entry when all mahr is deferred. In al-Khulasa that al-Ustadh Zahir al-Din used to give fatwa that she does not have the right to withhold, and al-Sadr al-Shahid used to give fatwa that she does. So fatwa differed. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: If the mahr is deferred, then the term arrives, she has no right to withhold according to Abu Hanifa. I did not see the ruling if the term was one year, for example, and she did not surrender herself until the term passed: does it become immediate? Or must there be a year after surrender as Abu Hanifa said in sale? For if marriage is analogized to sale, it is correct because they considered it so here. In al-Muhit and elsewhere: If a woman refers a man to her husband for the mahr (hawala), she has the right to withhold until the transferee receives because her debtor is like her agent. If the husband refers her for her mahr, she does not have the right to withhold. This is if the term is known. If it is unknown, if the ignorance is approximate like harvest, threshing, and the like, it is like known. These have forms: either explicit immediacy of all, or promptness, or immediacy of part and deferral of part, or deferral of all with a known term, or unknown, or approximate, or excessive. That is seven. Each either with condition of entry before receipt or not, that is fourteen. Each either the prohibition is before delivery or after, that is twenty-eight according to the correct view as in al-Zahiriyya, unlike sale where such condition is not permissible. If the ignorance is excessive, like 'until ease' or 'until wind blows' or 'until rain falls', the term is not established and the mahr is due immediately. Quoted in Ghayat al-Bayan. The apparent meaning is that deferral to divorce or death is excessive, so the wealth is due immediately by the implication of the absolute contract. The apparent contrary due to custom permitting such deferral, and it is mentioned in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya that there is a difference of opinion, and he affirmed that the ruling of deferral after the contract is like the ruling in it, as in Fath al-Qadir also. All this is if entry is not stipulated before the term. If they stipulate it and she consents, she has no right to withhold by agreement, as in al-Fath also. In al-Khulasa: By divorce the deferred becomes immediate, even if he takes her back it does not become deferred again. End quote. Meaning if the deferral is to divorce; but if the deferral is to a specified period, it does not become immediate by divorce, as occurs in Egypt in some marriages: they make part immediate, part deferred to divorce or death, and part in installments of a fixed amount each year. If he divorces her, the deferred part becomes immediate, not the installment part, because she takes it after divorce on its installments as she would have taken it before divorce on its installments. Two opinions are mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyya on the correct. The part either after the contract or not. His saying: (And custom is not considered when explicit stipulation contradicts it) Means she has the right to withhold until she receives all if they stipulated immediacy even if there is a custom of advancing part and deferring part; that custom is not considered because of explicit stipulation to the contrary. His saying: (In Mi'raj al-Diraya) al-Ramli said: This is a choice for the fatwa given by al-Ustadh Zahir al-Din, and its reasoning is that when the contract occurs necessitating her surrender before receiving the mahr due to deferral, this does not cease by the arrival of the term. Reflect. His saying: (She has no right to withhold by agreement) Nuh Afandi said: In the words of Qadikhan...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, provides detailed rulings on the wife's right to withhold herself from the husband (imtina') due to non-payment of mahr. The author begins by stating that the wife may withhold herself by removing obstacles (i.e., not surrendering) and that both spouses are equal in this regard before receiving mahr. He then clarifies that if the mahr is a specific item ('ayn), they should exchange it mutually as in barter sale, which he found in al-Muhit, and this corrects a misunderstanding in Fath al-Qadir. The author then explains that the husband cannot prevent the wife from going out for her needs or visiting before mahr is paid because she is not confined to his right until then; after payment she is confined. The father has the right to travel with his virgin daughter even if she is adult before the mahr is paid, but not after it is paid. Intercourse with her against her will before mahr is paid is not permissible if her refusal is for demanding mahr (according to Abu Hanifa), but if her refusal is for another reason, it is permissible because she is unjust. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ: they hold it permissible even if for mahr. The key ruling is about the wife's right to withhold: if the mahr is stipulated as immediate (hal) or prompt (mu'ajjal), she may withhold until she receives it all. If part is immediate and part deferred, she withholds until she receives the immediate part only. If the entire mahr is deferred, she has no right to withhold because she agreed to deferral. Abu Yusuf disagrees by istihsan: she may still withhold because the husband's request for deferral implies he waives his right to immediate consummation. Later, al-Walwaliji says fatwa is given by Abu Yusuf's view by istihsan, though fatwa differed between Zahir al-Din and al-Sadr al-Shahid. The passage then goes into many sub-cases: when the term is known or unknown, approximate or excessive; the effect of stipulating entry before receipt; the ruling on hawalat al-mahr (transfer of debt); and the effect of divorce on deferred mahr. For example, if the husband refers the wife to someone else for her mahr, she still withholds until the transferee receives; if the wife refers the husband to someone else, she does not withhold. If the term is excessively indefinite (e.g., 'until rain'), the term is invalid and mahr is due immediately. Deferral to divorce or death is considered valid because of custom. If entry is stipulated before the term and she consents, she cannot withhold by agreement. Divorce accelerates the deferred mahr if it was deferred to divorce, but not if it was a fixed period or installments. Throughout, the Hanafi school's reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas) to sale and istihsan, with attention to custom ('urf).

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower (bridal gift) that a husband must give to his wife as an obligatory part of the marriage contract.
امتناع (imtinā‘): The wife's legal right to refuse to surrender herself (for intercourse or leaving her home) until she receives her mahr.
تأجيل (ta’jīl): Deferring the payment of mahr to a future date as agreed in the contract.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that sets aside strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or general welfare.
قبض (qabḍ): Physical or constructive receipt/possession of the mahr by the wife or her agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if the entire mahr is stipulated as deferred (mu'ajjal), can the wife withhold herself from the husband?
A) Yes, she can withhold until she receives the mahr.
B) No, she cannot withhold because she waived her right by agreeing to deferral.
C) Yes, but only if she has not yet surrendered herself at all.
D) No, unless the husband fails to pay on the due date.

Key Takeaway
A wife's right to withhold for mahr is conditional on the mahr being immediately due; deferral waives the right under the dominant view, though Abu Yusuf allows it by istihsan.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Right to Withhold for Deferred Mahr: Dispute and Custom
Intra-Hanafi analysis of wife's right to withhold and role of custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on the wife's right to withhold when the mahr is deferred, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and determine the ruling when the contract is silent based on custom.

Core Idea
The wife may withhold for deferred mahr by istihsan; custom, not qiyas, governs when the contract is silent.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a wife can withhold herself from her husband when the mahr is deferred. Abu Hanifa analogizes marriage to sale, denying the right, but Abu Yusuf relies on istihsan and prevalent custom to allow it. The later fatwa adopts Abu Yusuf's view, and custom becomes decisive when the contract is silent. Understanding this shows how Hanafi fiqh balances textual analogy with social practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What is the wife's right to withhold (imtina') when the mahr is deferred and its term has expired? Is it analogous to sale or governed by custom?
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold that she cannot withhold after the term expires, using qiyas on sale: just as a seller cannot withhold delivery after a credit term, the wife must submit.
This is the position argued by analogy.
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view and his dalil
Abu Yusuf says she may withhold by istihsan, because custom ('adah) dictates that entry is delayed when the mahr is deferred. Custom overrides the analogy to sale.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi method of juristic preference.
4
Note the shift in fatwa
Later scholars (mutakhkhirin) such as al-Walwaliji adopted Abu Yusuf's view as the mufta bihi. This is now the relied-upon position.
The fatwa shifted due to the strength of custom.
5
Apply the custom principle when the contract is silent
When the contract does not specify whether the mahr is immediate or deferred, custom ('urf) of the locality determines. If custom is to defer part or all, the wife may withhold accordingly.
Principle: 'al-thabit bi al-'urf ka al-thabit bi al-shart'.

يمتنع ذلك بحلول الأجل تأمل قوله : (ليس لها الامتناع اتفاقاً قال نوح أفندي: في كلام قاضيخان روي، فما أن كونه بتعجل المؤجل بالطلاق الرجعي مطلقاً أو إلى انقضاء العدة. وجزم في القنية بأنه لا يحل إلى انقضاء العدة قال : وهو قول عامة مشايخنا وفي الصيرفية لو ارتدت ولحقت بدار الحرب ثم أسلمت وتزوجها المخترا أنه لا يطالب بالمهر المؤجل إلى الطلاق ا هـ. ووجهه الردة فسخ وليست بطلاق، وأما إذا سكتا عن وصفه فهو حال بمقتضى إطلاق العقد فالقياس على البيع يقتضي أن لها الامتناع قبل قبضه لكن العرف صرفه عن ذلك، فإن كان عرف في تعجيل بعضه وتأخير باقيه إلى الموت أو الميسرة أو الطلاق فليس لها الامتناع إلا إلى تسليم ذلك بتمامه ولو بقي درهم قال في فتاوى قاضيخان فإن لم يبينوا قدر المعجل ينظر إلى المرأة وإلى المهر أنه كم يكون المعجل لمثل هذه المرأة من مثل هذا المهر فيعجل ذلك، ولا يتقدر بالربع والخمس بل يعتبر المتعارف فإن الثابت عرفاً كالثابت شرطاً ا هـ . وفي الصيرفية : الفتوى على اعتبار عرف بلدهما من غير اعتبار الثلث أو النصف كما في غاية البيان من إطلاق قوله فإن كان يعني المهر بشرط التعجيل أو مسكوتاً عن يجب حالاً ولها أن تمنع نفسها حتى يعطيها المهر، إنما هو على ظاهر الرواية، وأما على المفتى به فالمعتبر في المسكوت عنه العرف وبه سقط ما في فتح القدير وفي القاسمية إذا تزوجها على مائة مثلاً على حكم الحلول على أن يعطيها قبل الدخول أربعين والباقي على حكمه فلها المطالبة بالباقي قبل الطلاق أو الموت ولها الامتناع حتى تقبضه وقول الزيعلي ليس لها أن تحبس نفسها فيما تعورف تأجيله ولو كان حالاً أنه ولو كان حالاً بمقتضى العقد فإن العرف يقضي به وبقية كلامه يدل عليه وهو قوله : فإذا نصا على تعجيل جميع المهر إلى آخره لأن شرط التعجيل مرادف لشرط الحلول حكماً لأن في كل منهما لها المطالبة متى شاءت ولو كان معناه، ولو كان حالاً بالشرط لناقض قوله وإن نصا على التعجيل فهو على ما شرطا وليس في اشتراط تعجيل البعض مع النص على حلول الجميع دليل على تأخير الباقي إلى الطلاق أو الموت بوجه من وجوه الدلالات والذي عليه العادة في مثل هذا التأخير إلى اختيار المطالبة . وقال الزاهدي وصار تأخير الصداق إلى الموت أو الطلاق بخوارزم عادة مأثورة وشريعة معروفة عندهم اهـ وعرف خوارزم فيما لا نص فيه على تعجيل ولا تأجيل وهو خلاف أداء ما يدل على الخلاف في هذ الصورة أيضاً فإنه قال : ولو كان كل المهر مؤجلاً وشرط الدخول قبل شيء كان له أن يدخل بها كما قال أبو حنيفة ومحمد ا هـ. فإنه يشعر بخلاف أبي يوسف قوله : وبه سقط ما في فتح القدير) أي من قوله بعد نقله عبارة الخانية ومثل هذا في غير نسخة من كتب الفقه فما وقع في غاية البيان من إطلاق قوله الخ ليس بواقع قوله : (وفي القاسمية) أي الفتاوى المنسوبة للعلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام قوله : (أنه لو كان حالاً بمقتضى العقد) أي معناه أو تأويله ولو كان حالاً الخ. وفي بعض النسخ أي بمقتضى العقد وهو أظهر لكن الذي رأيته في القاسمية ومعنى قوله ولو كان حالاً أنه ولو كان حالاً بمقتضى العقد.
The Book of Marriage, Chapter of Mahr. Immediate. Al-Walwaliji said: The fatwa is given according to Abu Yusuf's statement by way of istihsan, contrary to sale. Because custom is prevalent in delaying entry when all the mahr is deferred. In al-Khulasa: al-Ustadh Zahir al-Din used to give fatwa that he [the husband] does not have the right to withhold [her], while al-Sadr al-Shahid used to give fatwa that she has that right. So the fatwa differed. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: If the mahr is deferred and then the term expires, she does not have the right to withhold according to Abu Hanifa. I have not seen the ruling if the term was one year, for example, and she did not surrender herself until the term passed—does it become [due immediately] or must there be a year after surrender as Abu Hanifa said in sale? For if marriage is analogized to sale, it is valid because they considered it as such here. In al-Muhit and elsewhere: If a woman transfers a man to her husband for the mahr, she has the right to withhold until the transferee receives it because her creditor is like her agent. If the husband transfers her to someone for her mahr, she does not have the right to withhold. This is when the term is known. If it is unknown, if the ignorance is minor like harvest and threshing and the like, it is like known. These are of several types: either they specify the whole as immediate or prompt, or part immediate and part deferred, or all deferred with a known term, or unknown, or minor, or excessive. So they are seven. Each of them either with the condition of entry before receipt or not, so they are fourteen. Each of them either with prohibition before surrender or after, so they are twenty-eight according to the correct view as in al-Zahiriyya, contrary to sale which is not valid with this condition. If it is excessive like 'until ease' or 'until the wind blows' or 'until the sky rains', the term is not established and the mahr is due immediately. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. Its apparent meaning is that deferment to divorce or death is excessive, so the mahr is due immediately by virtue of the absolute contract. But the apparent contrary is due to custom of deferment being practiced. In al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya a difference is mentioned, and it is corrected that the ruling of deferment after the contract is like its ruling in the contract, as also in Fath al-Qadir. All this is if they did not stipulate entry before the term expires. If they stipulate it and she agrees, she does not have the right to withhold by agreement, as in al-Fath. In al-Khulasa: By divorce the deferred becomes immediate, and if he returns to her it is not deferred again. Meaning if the deferment was to divorce. But if the deferment was to a specific period, it is not accelerated by divorce, as occurs in the land of Egypt in some marriages where they make part immediate, part deferred to divorce or death, and part in installments each year a fixed amount. So if he divorces her, the deferred part becomes immediate, not the installment, because she takes it after divorce in its installments as she would before divorce. Two opinions are mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyya in the correct part. The part is either after the contract or not. His statement: 'There is no consideration of custom when explicit wording contradicts it' means she has the right to withhold until she receives the whole if they stipulated immediate payment even if there was a custom of paying part promptly and deferring part; that custom is not considered due to the explicit contrary. His statement: 'In Mi'raj al-Diraya' al-Ramli said: This is a choice for what al-Ustadh Zahir al-Din gave fatwa on, and its reasoning is that since the contract necessitates her surrender before receipt of the mahr due to deferment, that is not prevented by the expiry of the term. Consider. His statement: 'She does not have the right to withhold by agreement.' Nuh Afandi said: In the words of Qadikhan it is narrated... that it accelerates the deferred [mahr] by revocable divorce absolutely or until the end of the waiting period. In al-Qunyah it is decided that it does not become due until the end of the waiting period, and he said it is the statement of the majority of our scholars. In al-Sayrafiyya: If she apostatized and joined the abode of war, then became Muslim and married someone else, he is not asked for the mahr deferred to divorce. Its reasoning is that apostasy is dissolution and not divorce. As for when they are silent about its description, it is immediate by virtue of the absolute contract. Analogy on sale would require that she has the right to withhold before receipt, but custom diverts from that. If there is a custom of promptly paying part and deferring the remainder to death, ease, or divorce, she does not have the right to withhold except until that is fully delivered, even if a dirham remains. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: If they do not specify the amount of the prompt portion, one looks to the woman and the mahr to see what amount would be prompt for such a woman from such a mahr, and that is to be given promptly. It is not apportioned by a quarter or a fifth; rather, the customary practice is considered, for what is established by custom is like what is established by condition. In al-Sayrafiyya: The fatwa is on considering the custom of their town, without considering one-third or one-half, as in Ghayat al-Bayan from the absolute wording of his statement: 'If he means the mahr with the condition of promptness, or it is silent about it, it is due immediately and she may withhold herself until he gives her the mahr.' That is only according to the apparent narration. As for the mufta bihi, the consideration in the silent case is custom, and by this what is in Fath al-Qadir is refuted. In al-Qasimiyya: If he marries her for a hundred, for example, on the basis of immediate payment, on condition that he gives her forty before entry and the remainder on its basis, she may demand the remainder before divorce or death and she may withhold until she receives it. The statement of al-Zayla'i that she may not withhold herself in what is customarily deferred even if it is immediate? That 'even if it is immediate by virtue of the contract' because custom rules over it. The rest of his speech indicates that, which is his statement: 'If they specify the prompt payment of the entire mahr...' to the end, because the condition of promptness is synonymous with the condition of immediate payment in ruling, because in each she may demand whenever she wishes. Even if it was immediate by condition would contradict his statement. And if they stipulate promptness, it is as they stipulated. There is no evidence in stipulating promptness of part with specification of the entire amount being immediate for deferring the remainder to divorce or death in any way. What is customary in such deferment is to option of demand. Al-Zahidi said: The deferment of the sadaq to death or divorce in Khwarazm became a transmitted custom and a known tradition among them. The custom of Khwarazm regarding what has no text on promptness or deferment is contrary. Performance indicates the difference in this form as well, for he said: 'If all the mahr was deferred and he stipulated entry before anything, he may enter with her as Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said.' This suggests the disagreement of Abu Yusuf. His statement: 'And by this what is in Fath al-Qadir is refuted' that is from his statement after quoting the phrase of al-Khaniyya. And such is in other copies of the books of fiqh. So what occurred in Ghayat al-Bayan from the absolute wording of his statement etc. is not a reality. His statement: 'In al-Qasimiyya,' that is the fatawa attributed to al-Allama Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, student of al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam. His statement: 'That even if it was immediate by virtue of the contract' means its meaning or interpretation. In some copies: 'immediate by virtue of the contract' is clearer. But what I saw in al-Qasimiyya, and the meaning of his statement 'even if it was immediate' is that even if it was immediate by virtue of the contract.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the wife's right to withhold herself from her husband until she receives the mahr (dower). The commentary opens by stating the dispute: although the default rule in sale is that the seller cannot withhold after the term expires, in marriage Abu Yusuf's view (by istihsan) is adopted as the fatwa, allowing the wife to withhold when the mahr is deferred. The reason given is that custom dictates delaying entry when the full mahr is deferred. The author then presents various scenarios: known vs. unknown terms, minor vs. excessive ignorance, and the effect of stipulating entry before payment. A key point is that when the mahr is deferred to an excessive event (like 'until ease' or 'until death'), the deferment is invalid and the mahr becomes due immediately. However, custom overrides this if deferment to death or divorce is common. The text further discusses cases where the contract is silent: the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that custom determines the ruling. Thus, if local custom dictates that part of the mahr is prompt and part deferred, the wife may withhold until she receives the deferred portion in full. The passage also covers the effect of divorce: if the mahr is deferred to divorce, it accelerates; if deferred to a fixed term, it does not. Finally, the author notes that the fatwa considers the 'urf (custom) of the locality, refuting some earlier texts.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife, either immediate or deferred.
الامتناع (al-imtina'): The wife's right to physically withhold herself from her husband until she receives the mahr.
التأجيل (al-ta'jil): Deferment of the mahr payment to a future date or event.
العرف (al-'urf): Customary practice that determines rulings when the contract is silent.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling based on custom or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, when a marriage contract is silent about whether the mahr is immediate or deferred, what determines the wife's right to withhold?
A) The mahr is considered immediate, so she can withhold until received.
B) The mahr is considered deferred, so she cannot withhold.
C) Custom of the locality determines the ruling.
D) She must ask the qadi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi allows the wife to withhold for deferred mahr, and custom fills the gap when the contract is silent.

Default Promptness of Mahr and Effect of Custom
Ruling on when mahr is prompt by default and how custom overrides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling on promptness of mahr in Hanafi fiqh and explain how custom ('urf) modifies this ruling, citing the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Default mahr is prompt, but custom can defer part; the wife's right to withhold is limited to the prompt portion.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a crucial matter in marriage contracts: when the mahr (dower) is not specified as prompt or deferred, what is the default? The Hanafi school begins with an analogy to sale: like price, the mahr is due immediately. However, local custom can change this default. Understanding the interplay between the default and custom is essential for accurately determining the rights of both spouses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling and its proof
State that unspecified mahr is prompt by default, based on qiyas on sale (bay'). The proof is analogy: in sale, price is due immediately unless deferred.
This is the qiyas jaliy (evident analogy).
2
Recognize the role of custom as an override
Custom can turn away from the default. If the local custom divides the mahr into prompt and deferred parts, the wife cannot withhold for the deferred part.
Custom ('urf) overrides qiyas as a form of istihsan.
3
Determine the prompt portion when unspecified
According to Fatawa Qadikhan, the prompt portion is determined by looking at the custom for such a woman and such a mahr; it is not a fixed fraction like a quarter or half.
The custom of the town is the criterion.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The fatwa (mufta bihi) is to consider custom, not the apparent riwaya (zahir al-riwaya) which assumes full promptness.
The text states: 'al-fatwa 'ala i'tibar al-'urf' (the fatwa is on considering custom).
5
Distinguish between zahir al-riwaya and mufta bihi
Zahir al-riwaya says unspecified mahr is fully prompt and wife can withhold until full payment. Mufta bihi says custom determines the prompt portion.
This is an intra-Hanafi shift in operative ruling.

End quote.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on mahr (dower) when the contract does not specify whether it is prompt (hal) or deferred (mu'ajjal). The default rule, based on analogy to sale (qiyas 'ala al-bay'), is that the mahr is due immediately (hal). In a sale, the price is due upon contract unless deferred; similarly, the mahr is due promptly, and the wife has the right to withhold herself (habs) until she receives it. However, custom ('urf) overrides this default. If local custom divides the mahr into a prompt portion and a deferred portion (to death, divorce, or ease), the wife may only withhold for the prompt part, not the deferred. The text cites Fatawa Qadikhan: if the prompt amount is unspecified, it is determined by custom, not by a fixed fraction like one-fourth or one-half. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that custom is the primary consideration, not the apparent riwaya (zahir al-riwaya). The text also discusses a scenario where the parties stipulate part prompt and part deferred; the wife can demand the deferred portion before divorce or death if she chooses, as per al-Zayla'i. The custom of Khwarazm is noted as deferring the dower entirely to death or divorce. Additionally, if the husband divorces before consummation after specifying a prompt portion but being silent on the deferred, she gets half the named mahr and should receive mut'ah (compensation).

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift; specified consideration in the marriage contract.
حال (hal): Prompt; immediately due and payable upon the contract.
مؤجل (mu'ajjal): Deferred; payment delayed to a specified future event (e.g., death, divorce).
العرف (al-'urf): Custom; local practice that can modify the default legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, if the marriage contract does not specify whether the mahr is prompt or deferred, what determines the prompt portion?
A) Half of the mahr is always prompt
B) The local custom ('urf) of the town
C) The wife's family decides
D) The husband chooses

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that custom ('urf) determines the prompt portion of mahr, overriding the default analogy to sale.

Wife's Right to Withhold After Consensual Intercourse: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife's right to withhold after consensual intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the wife's right to withhold after consensual intercourse and apply each position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
After consensual intercourse, Abu Hanifa says the wife may still withhold; the Sahibayn say she cannot — the dispute turns on whether each act is a separate disposal.

The wife's right to withhold herself (habs) until she receives her mahr is a well-known remedy. But what happens after she has already engaged in intercourse or valid seclusion with consent? The Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa retains her right, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it drops. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position through a careful analysis of the text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed and disputed scenarios
The passage first clarifies that when the wife is coerced, a minor, or insane, there is no dispute: her right to withhold remains. The dispute only arises when she is adult and consents to intercourse or seclusion.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that the wife may still withhold. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that she loses this right because the full mahr is confirmed by the first act.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They analogize to a seller who delivers the sold item: after delivery, the seller cannot withhold the item. Similarly, intercourse/seclusion delivers the entire object of the contract, so the wife cannot withhold.
The object is the usufruct of the vulva.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof and response
Abu Hanifa uses a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) to a slave who commits multiple crimes: each crime demands the slave as compensation. Each act of intercourse is a separate disposal of the vulva deserving compensation, so the right to withhold remains for subsequent acts.
The first act confirms the mahr only due to ignorance of future acts.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife can refuse further intercourse until the mahr is paid. Under the Sahibayn, she cannot. The later fatwa of Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar distinguishes between staying and travel: in staying, follow Sahibayn; in travel, follow Abu Hanifa.
This shows a practical reconciliation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في قوله فإن وطئها فشمل ما إذا وطئها مكرهة كانت أو صغيرة أو برضاها وهي كبيرة ولا خلاف فيما إذا كانت مكرهة أو صبية أو مجنونة فإنه لا يسقط حقها في الحبس، وأما إذا وطئها أو خلا بها برضاها ففيه خلاف. قال أبو حنيفة : لها أن تمنع نفسها وخالفاه لأن المعقود عليه كله صار مسلماً إليه بالوطأة الواحدة وبالخلوة، ولهذا يتأكد بها جميع المهر فلم يبق لها حق الحبس كالبائع إذا سلم المبيع. وله أنها منعت منه ما قابل البدل لأن كل وطأة تصرف في البضع المحترم فلا يعرى عن العوض إبانة لخطره، والتأكد بالواحدة لجهالة ما وارءها فلا يصلح مزاحماً للمعلوم. ثم إذا وجد آخر وصار معلوماً تحققت المزاحمة وصار المهر مقابلاً بالكل كالعبد إذا جنى جناية يدفع كله بها، ثم إذا جنى جناية أخرى وأخرى يدفع بجميعها
And his statement is general: 'if he has intercourse with her' so it includes if he has intercourse with her whether coerced, minor, or with her consent while she is adult. There is no disagreement when she is coerced, a girl, or insane: her right to withhold does not drop. But if he has intercourse with her or secludes himself with her with her consent, there is disagreement. Abu Hanifa said: she may withhold herself, and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opposed him, because the object of the contract has all been delivered to him by one act of intercourse and by seclusion, and therefore the entire mahr becomes confirmed by it, so she has no right to withhold, like the seller when he delivers the sold item. And he (Abu Hanifa) has the proof that she prevented from him what was in exchange for the consideration because every act of intercourse disposes of the venerable vulva and is not devoid of compensation to indicate its importance. The confirmation by one act is due to ignorance of what is beyond it, so it cannot compete with the known. Then if another occurs and becomes known, the competition occurs and the mahr becomes fully exchangeable for the entire set, like a slave who commits a crime: he is surrendered entirely for it, then if he commits another and another, he is surrendered for them all.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to withhold herself (habs) for the mahr after intercourse or valid seclusion (khalwa). All scholars agree that if intercourse was coerced, or the wife was a minor or insane, her right to withhold is not affected—she can still demand the mahr before surrendering herself again. The dispute arises when the wife is adult and consents to intercourse or seclusion. Abu Hanifa holds that she retains the right to withhold herself until she receives the mahr, because each act of intercourse is a separate disposal of the 'budd' (vulva) that deserves compensation; the first act does not waive the right for future acts. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that intercourse or seclusion transfers the entire object of the contract (the usufruct of the vulva) to the husband, making all the mahr due immediately, similar to a seller who delivers the sold item—he cannot then refuse further delivery. Abu Hanifa responds with an analogy: like a slave who commits multiple crimes (jinayat), each crime demands the slave as compensation; the first crime does not exhaust the right of later claimants. Similarly, each act of intercourse is a separate use deserving compensation, and the first act's confirmation of part of the mahr does not eliminate the right to withhold for the remainder.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): The wife's right to withhold herself (refuse to be available to the husband) until she receives her mahr.
الخلوة (al-khalwa): Valid seclusion (privacy) between spouses after marriage that is lawful and free from legal impediments; it triggers the same effects as actual intercourse in some rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does the wife retain the right to withhold herself after consensual intercourse?
A) Because the mahr is not yet fully paid
B) Because each act of intercourse is a separate disposal deserving compensation, like a slave's multiple crimes
C) Because the husband has not yet consummated the marriage
D) Because the wife never loses her right regardless of circumstances

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to withhold after consensual intercourse is disputed among Hanafis: Abu Hanifa retains it, the Sahibayn drop it, and later practice distinguishes between travel and non-travel contexts.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Nafaqah: Domestic vs. Travel Withholding
Consequence of the ikhtilaf on nafaqah and a practical fatwa distinguishing stay and travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on nafaqah when a wife withholds for mahr, and apply the mufta bihi distinction between domestic and travel scenarios.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi distinguishes domestic withholding (Sahibayn) from travel withholding (Abu Hanifa) — nafaqah preserved only in travel.

Earlier, we saw the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a wife who withholds herself for the mahr is nashiz. This dispute has a direct practical effect: does she lose her maintenance? In this passage, the commentator derives the consequence and presents a fatwa practice that splits the difference. Understanding this refined position is essential for a mufti navigating between the Hanafi imams' views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its immediate consequence
Locate the two positions: Abu Hanifa holds the wife is not nashiz and gets nafaqah; Sahibayn hold she is nashiz and loses nafaqah.
The consequence is stated directly: 'عنده تستحقها ... وعندهما لا تستحقها'.
2
Note the qualification for Sahibayn's position
Even according to the Sahibayn, if she withholds from intercourse but remains in the marital home after receiving the mahr, she is not nashiz. This limits the scope of their disagreement.
The text says: 'لا تكون ناشزة على قولهما إذا منعته من الوطء وهي في بيته'.
3
Understand the fatwa distinction by al-Saffar
Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar distinguishes two contexts: domestic withholding (preventing intercourse after consummation) and travel withholding (refusing to travel for mahr). For domestic, he follows Sahibayn (no nafaqah); for travel, he follows Abu Hanifa (nafaqah maintained).
Al-Bazdawi approves this as 'حسن في الفتيا' (good in fatwa).
4
Apply the distinction to analogous cases
Consider scenarios where the mahr is defective or the wife buys something that is reclaimed. The text cites Abu Yusuf's view that she cannot withhold in those cases. Also note the difference between relocation (tabwi') within the same city/village and travel to a distant place; only the latter triggers the Abu Hanifa position.
The passage also touches on the mu'nisa (attendant) obligation, clarifying it is not obligatory despite the initial statement.
