Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq derives the practical consequence of the earlier ikhtilaf on maintenance (nafaqah). According to Abu Hanifa, a wife who withholds herself for the mahr is not recalcitrant (nashiz) and is entitled to maintenance. According to the Sahibayn, she is nashiz and loses maintenance. However, the text qualifies that even according to the Sahibayn, if she merely prevents intercourse while staying in the house (not traveling), she should not be considered nashiz after having received the mahr. The text then cites a practical fatwa from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar: in matters of preventing intercourse (after consummation), he would give fatwa according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (i.e., she cannot withhold, and if she does, no maintenance). But in matters of travel, he would give fatwa according to Abu Hanifa (i.e., she can withhold from traveling to demand the mahr and still get maintenance). This distinction is praised as 'good in fatwa.' The passage also discusses scenarios regarding the quality of mahr received. According to Abu Yusuf (no mention of Imam), if the mahr is found to be counterfeited or defective, or if the wife bought something which was then reclaimed, she cannot withhold herself because she voluntarily received it. Regarding the husband's right to transfer the wife: moving within the same city or to a village counts as relocation (tabwi'), not travel, and he can do so by agreement; moving to a rural area (rustaq) is disputed. The text ends with a note about the mu'nisa (attendant) obligation, indicating it is not obligatory.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance; financial support the husband must provide to the wife, including food, clothing, housing.
النشوز (al-nushuz): Legal recalcitrance; the wife's unjustified refusal of the husband's rights, which can result in loss of maintenance.
التبوئة (al-tabwi'): Relocation; moving to a new dwelling without being considered travel (safar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She retains her maintenance because she is acting on Abu Hanifa's view
C) She becomes nashiz and must be divorced
D) The husband can force her

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for nafaqah when a wife withholds for mahr distinguishes domestic withholding (no nafaqah, following Sahibayn) from travel withholding (nafaqah due, following Abu Hanifa).

Ruling on Prompt Mahr and Divorce Before Consummation
Ruling on mahr when only prompt portion is named and divorce before consummation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when only prompt mahr is named and divorce occurs before consummation, and identify the wife's entitlement to half the named mahr and mut'ah.

Core Idea
When only prompt mahr is named and divorce before consummation, half the named mahr plus mut'ah is due.

This lesson presents a specific scenario within Hanafi marriage law: a husband specifies only the prompt portion of the mahr (mu'ajjal) and remains silent about the deferred portion (mu'ajjal), then divorces before consummation. The ruling from al-Sayrifya clarifies the wife's entitlement to half the named prompt mahr and also mentions the appropriateness of mut'ah (a consolatory gift). This is a clear ruling that serves as a memorization anchor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband names only the prompt mahr (e.g., 100) and is silent about the deferred portion. He then divorces her before any consummation.
2
Determine the primary entitlement
The wife receives half of the named prompt mahr (e.g., 50). This is an obligatory right (wajib).
Half of the prompt mahr is due because the marriage was not consummated.
3
Note the additional entitlement
It is appropriate (mustahab) that the husband also gives mut'ah (a consolatory gift).
Mut'ah is recommended, not wajib.
4
Recognize the authority
This ruling comes from later Hanafi works (al-Sayrifya) and is consistent with the madhhab's principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الصيرفية : تزوجها وسمى لها المعجل مائة وسكت عن المؤجل ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فلها نصف المسمى وينبغي أن تجب لها المتعة .اهـ.
And in al-Sayrifya: He married her and named for her the prompt portion as one hundred and was silent about the deferred portion, then divorced her before consummation, so she gets half of the named amount, and it is appropriate that mut'ah should be due for her. End.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a case where the husband specifies only the prompt portion of the mahr (mu'ajjal) and remains silent about the deferred portion (mu'ajjal). If he then divorces her before consummation, she is entitled to half of the named prompt mahr. Additionally, she should also receive mut'ah (a compensatory gift) as appropriate. This is a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school, and it is a memorization anchor for students. The authority weight: this ruling appears in later fatawa works (al-Sayrifya) but is consistent with the madhhab's principles.

Key Terms
المعجل (al-mu'ajjal): The prompt portion of the mahr, payable immediately upon marriage.
المؤجل (al-mu'ajjal): The deferred portion of the mahr, payable at a later date or upon divorce/death.
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to the wife upon divorce before consummation, over and above the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half of the named prompt mahr (50) plus mut'ah
C) Nothing, because mahr was not fully specified
D) The entire deferred mahr as well

Key Takeaway
When only prompt mahr is named and divorce occurs before consummation, the wife receives half the named prompt mahr and mut'ah is appropriate.

Wife's Right to Prevent Intercourse: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute with qiyas argument and fatwa resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the wife's right to prevent intercourse after consummation, and state the practical consequences for maintenance according to each view.

Core Idea
Even after consummation, the wife may retain her right to prevent intercourse until the mahr is fully paid.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the wife's right to prevent herself from intercourse (habs) after the marriage has been consummated. While all agree she can prevent before consummation, a disagreement arises after one act of intercourse or seclusion with consent. Abu Hanifa holds she retains the right for each subsequent act, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that the right is lost after the first act. This conflict has important implications for the wife's entitlement to maintenance (nafaqah) if she prevents further intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the undisputed cases
Note that when the wife is coerced, a minor, or insane, there is no disagreement: her right of prevention is not dropped.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Abu Hanifa holds that the wife retains the right to prevent after each act of intercourse until the full mahr is paid.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that after one consensual act or seclusion, the wife loses the right to prevent, as the entire mahr becomes confirmed.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Understand Abu Hanifa's qiyas (analogy) of a slave who commits multiple crimes – each crime requires full compensation. For the Sahibayn, the analogy is a seller who delivers goods – once delivered, the seller cannot reclaim them.
5
Apply to maintenance
According to Abu Hanifa, the wife who prevents is not nashiz and deserves maintenance. According to the Sahibayn, she is nashiz and loses maintenance.
6
Consider the fatwa resolution
Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar combined the views: for prevention after consummation, follow the Sahibayn; for travel (safar) to seek mahr, follow Abu Hanifa. This is considered good in fatwa.

And he made absolute in his statement: 'if he has intercourse with her,' so it includes when he has intercourse with her whether coerced, or a minor, or with her consent while she is an adult. There is no dispute when she is coerced, a child, or insane, for her right of prevention is not dropped. As for when he has intercourse with her or secluded with her with her consent, there is disagreement. Abu Hanifa said: She can prevent herself. But they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed because the entire subject of the contract is delivered to him by one act of intercourse and by seclusion, and therefore the entire mahr becomes confirmed by it, so she no longer has the right of prevention, like a seller when he delivers the sold item. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is that she prevented from him what is equivalent to the compensation, because each act of intercourse is a disposal of the respected private part, so it is not devoid of consideration to show its significance. The confirmation by one (act) is due to the unknown nature of what follows, so it cannot compete with the known. Then when another appears and becomes known, competition is realized and the mahr becomes in exchange for the whole, like a slave who commits a crime; he is given as full payment for it, then if he commits another crime and another, he is given for all. And upon this difference is built the entitlement to maintenance after prevention. According to him (Abu Hanifa), she deserves it and is not rebellious, but according to them, she does not deserve it and is rebellious. Thus they said. It should be that she is not rebellious according to them when she prevents him from intercourse while she is in his house, because it is not rebellion from her after taking the mahr, as they explicitly stated in the chapters on maintenance. And in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Bazdawi: Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar used to give fatwa on prevention according to the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and on travel according to the opinion of Abu Hanifa. Then he said: 'This is good in fatwa,' meaning after consummation she should not prevent herself, and if she prevents, she has no maintenance as per their madhhab, and he should not travel with her, and she has the right to prevent him for seeking the mahr, and she has maintenance as per his madhhab, as in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) regarding the wife's right to prevent herself (habs) from intercourse after consummation or seclusion. The ruling is analyzed in the context of the phrase 'if he has intercourse with her.' The text first distinguishes cases where the wife is coerced, minor, or insane (no disagreement that her right remains). The dispute is when she consents. Abu Hanifa maintains that she can still prevent further acts if the mahr is unpaid, because each act of intercourse is a disposal of the respected private part that requires compensation. He uses a qiyas (analogy) of a slave who commits multiple crimes: the slave is given as full compensation for each crime, just as the wife's right to prevent is retained for each act. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the entire subject of the marriage (the bida') is delivered by the first act, so the mahr becomes fully confirmed, and she loses the right of prevention like a seller who delivers the goods. This leads to a difference in nafaqah (maintenance): according to Abu Hanifa, she still gets maintenance and is not nashiz (rebellious); according to them, she is nashiz and loses maintenance. The text also notes that if she prevents him while in his house after taking the mahr, she is not nashiz even according to them. Finally, it reports a fatwa from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar who combined the views: on prevention after consummation, he follows Sahibayn (no prevention, no maintenance); on travel (safar), he follows Abu Hanifa (she can prevent and has maintenance). This is presented as good in fatwa.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): The wife's right to prevent herself from intercourse until the mahr is paid.
النشوز (al-nushuz): In this context, a wife being rebellious by preventing intercourse without a valid reason, leading to loss of maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis of Abu Hanifa's view that the wife retains the right to prevent after each act?
A) The mahr is not confirmed until the entire amount is paid.
B) Each act of intercourse is like a separate disposal requiring compensation, analogous to a slave given for multiple crimes.
C) The marriage contract allows the wife to refuse intercourse at any time.
D) The Sahibayn's view is rejected because it weakens the wife's rights.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to prevent intercourse after consummation is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa allows it for each act; Sahibayn deny it after the first act, and the later fatwa combines their views depending on the context.

Wife's Right to Prevent Relocation: The Shift from Zahir al-Riwaya to Later Fatwa
Discusses the wife's right to prevent being taken out of her home or city, with differing fatwas based on changing circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's right to prevent relocation and explain how the later fatwa overrides the apparent ruling based on the principle of preventing harm.

Core Idea
The husband's right to move his wife is constrained by the Quranic prohibition of causing harm.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a crucial question in marriage: can a husband move his wife to another city without her consent? The Hanafi school's position evolved over time. Initially, the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya) gave the husband this right, citing the Quranic command to lodge wives where the husband lives. However, later scholars, seeing corruption of the times and the potential for harm, issued a fatwa restricting this right. This lesson traces that development and explains the fatwa that prevails today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two relocation scenarios
The passage distinguishes between moving within the same city (consensus she cannot prevent) and moving to another city/village. Focus on the latter as it is disputed.
2
Extract the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya)
According to early texts (al-Khaniyya, al-Walwalijiyya), the wife cannot prevent relocation based on Quran 65:6. Note that no distinction is made between safe and unsafe conditions.
The verse: 'Lodge them where you lodge, according to your means.'
3
Identify the later fatwa and its basis
Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth ruled that the husband cannot travel with her at all without her consent due to corrupted times. This is based on the Quranic clause 'do not make difficulties for them' (65:6), which prohibits harm. Taking her away causes harm.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
Later scholars (e.g., author of al-Mukhtar, many mashayikh) preferred the later fatwa. The passage shows that this choice is not against the Quran because the verse itself conditions the husband's right on absence of harm. The mufta bihi is the absolute prohibition without her consent.
This is a case of fatwa changing with time (ikhtilaf al-hukm bi ikhtilaf al-zaman).
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Imagine a husband wants to move his wife from Cairo to a distant village for work. According to the preferred fatwa, he cannot do so without her consent. The wife has the right to prevent because of likely harm (ghurba, insecurity).

And the author indicated by his statement 'and she has right to prevent him' that she is an adult. If she were...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the wife's right to prevent being taken out of her home or city by her husband (relocation). The text begins with a restriction: the wife cannot prevent intercourse or exit after she has received the mahr. The main focus is on the husband's request to move her. The passage first clarifies that moving within the same city is allowed by consensus. Moving between city and village is also considered permissible according to the apparent ruling of al-Kafi, but later sources show difference. For moving from one city to another, the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya) from al-Khaniyya and al-Walwalijiyya relies on the Quranic verse (65:6) 'Lodge them where you lodge' and says the wife cannot prevent. However, due to corruption of the times (fasad al-zaman), later scholars like Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth issued fatwas that the husband cannot travel with her without her consent at all. This is based on the context of the verse which includes 'do not make difficulties for them' (65:6), and taking her to another land causes harm. The passage also mentions that some scholars conditioned the husband's right on paying the prompt mahr and being trustworthy. Ultimately, the preferred fatwa (mufta bihi) is the opinion of the two jurists (al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth) that he cannot travel with her absolutely without her consent, and this is the practice of judges in later times. The text also notes that the ruling is subject to change based on time and circumstances. The passage concludes by noting that the author of the matn indicated that the wife's right to prevent is for an adult woman.

Key Terms
الغربة (al-ghurba): The state of being in a strange place away from one's home town, considered harmful for the wife.
المؤنسة (al-mu'nisah): A female companion for the wife, mentioned in the context of the legal house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred fatwa (mufta bihi) in later Hanafi scholarship, can a husband travel with his wife to another city without her consent?
A) Yes, based on the apparent meaning of Quran 65:6
B) No, because it causes harm (darar) to her, which is prohibited
C) Only if he pays all the mahr
D) Only if she is not an adult

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on wife's relocation shifted from allowing it under zahir al-riwaya to prohibiting without consent due to the Quranic condition of no harm and changing times.

Wife's Right to Refuse Travel: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's right to travel with wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling allows a wife to refuse travel without her consent and evaluate the earlier opposing position.

Core Idea
A husband cannot force his wife to travel; the fatwa changed to prevent harm in corrupt times.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a pivotal intra-Hanafi dispute: does a husband have the right to compel his wife to travel or move? The earlier transmitted ruling (zahir al-riwayah) granted him that right based on a Quranic command. However, later scholars, citing changing times and the principle of avoiding harm, reversed the ruling. This lesson walks through the arguments, the shift in fatwa, and the operative rule today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act in question is the husband's forcing his wife to travel from her city to another. Identify the two opposing rulings: the earlier position (husband's right) and the later mufta bihi (wife's right to refuse).
Focus on the change over time.
2
Locate the Dalil from Both Sides
Both sides use the same verse: Quran 65:6. The earlier position emphasizes 'House them where you are housed' as a command for the wife to follow. The later position emphasizes 'And do not harm them' as a condition that limits the command.
The verse is used for different parts.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The earlier ruling derives authority from the imperative 'askunuhunna' (house them) implying the husband's right to choose residence. The later ruling argues that the prohibition of harm ('la tudarruhunna') in the same verse restricts that right when travel causes harm.
The later scholars also invoke istihsan and 'urf.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf and the Tarjih
The dispute is intra-Hanafi: Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth opposed the earlier view. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the later fatwa, adopted by many mashayikh and judges, is the relied-upon position.
The tarjih is based on change of times and harm prevention.
5
Evaluate the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: under the mufta bihi, the wife has the right to refuse travel; the husband cannot compel her, even if he has paid the mahr.
This applies to adult wives; for minors, the guardian's rights are discussed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتب أنه ليس له ذلك ثم عزا إلى غيرها أن له ذلك قال : وهو الصواب اهـ. وأما إذا طلب انتقالها من مصرها إلى مصر أخرى فظاهر الرواية كما في الخانية والولوالجية أن ليس لها الامتناع لقوله تعالى اسكنوهن من حيث سكنتم من وجدكم [الطلاق: ٦] وليس في ظاهر الرواية تفصيل بين أن يكون مأموناً عليها أو لا. واختلفوا في المفتى به فذكر في جامع الفصولين أن الفتوى على أنه له أن يسافر بها إذا أوفاها المعجل .اهـ. فهذا إفتاء بظاهر الرواية، وأفتى أبو القاسم الصفار وتبعه الفقيه أبو الليث بأنه ليس له أن يسافر بها مطلقاً بغير رضاها لفساد الزمان لأنها لا تأمن على نفسها في منزلها فكيف إذا خرجت؟ وصرح في المختار بأنه لا يسافر بها وعليه الفتوى وفي المحيط وهو المختار وما في فصول الأستروشني معزياً إلى ظهير الدين المرغيناني من أن الأخذ بقول الله تعالى أولى من الأخذ بقول الفقيه فقد رده في غاية البيان بأن قول الفقيه ليس منافياً لقول الله تعالى لأن النص معلول بعدم الإضرار ألا ترى إلى سياق الآية وهو قوله تعالى ولا تضاروهن) [الطلاق: ٦] وفي إخراجها إلى غير بلدها إضرار بها فلا يجوز .اهـ. وذكر الولوالجي أن جواب ظاهر الرواية كان في زمانهم، أما في زماننا لا يملك الزوج ذلك فجعله من باب اختلاف الحكم باختلاف العصر والزمان كما قالوا في مسألة الاستئجار على الطاعات وأفتى بعضهم بأنه إذا أوفاها المعجل والمؤجل وكان مأموناً يسافر بها وإلا فلا لأن التأجيل إنما يثبت بحكم العرف فلعلها إنما رضيت بالتأجيل لأجل إمساكها في بلدها، أما إذا أخرجها إلى دار الغربة فلا. قال صاحب المجمع في شرحه وبه يفتي اهـ. فقد اختلف الإفتاء والأحسن الإفتاء بقول الفقيهين من غير تفصيل، واختاره كثير من المشايخ كما في الكافي وعليه الفتوى وعليه عمل القضاة في زماننا كما في أنفع الوسائل. وأشار المصنف بقوله ولها منعه إلى أنها بالغة، فلو كانت صغيرة فللولي المنع المذكور حتى يقبض مهرها وتسليمها نفسها غير صحيح فللولي استردادها، وليس لغير الأب والجد أن يسلمها إلى الزوج قبل أن يقبض الصداق من له ولاية قبضه، فإن سلمها فهو فاسد وترد إلى بيتها كما في التجنيس وغيره.
It was written that he does not have that right, then he attributed to others that he has that right, and he said: and that is correct. As for if she requests moving from her city to another city, then in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), as in al-Khaniya and al-Walwaljiya, that she does not have the right to refuse due to the saying of Allah the Most High: 'House them where you are housed' [65:6], and in the apparent transmission there is no distinction between whether she is safe or not. They differed on the fatwa: in Jami' al-Fusulayn it is mentioned that the fatwa is that he has the right to travel with her if he pays the prompt (mu'ajjal). So this is a fatwa according to the apparent transmission. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar gave a fatwa, followed by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, that he absolutely does not have the right to travel with her without her consent due to the corruption of the time, because she is not safe in her own home, so how if she goes out? It is explicitly stated in al-Mukhtar that he should not travel with her, and upon that is the fatwa, and in al-Muhit it is the chosen view. As for what is in Fusul al-Ustruwshini, attributed to Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani, that taking the saying of Allah the Most High is more worthy than taking the saying of the faqih, he refuted it in Ghayat al-Bayan by saying that the saying of the faqih is not contrary to the saying of Allah the Most High because the text is conditioned by the absence of harm; do you not see the context of the verse, which is His saying: 'And do not harm them' [65:6]? And in taking her out to a place other than her city there is harm, so it is not permissible. Al-Walwalji mentioned that the answer of the apparent transmission was in their time; as for our time, the husband does not possess that right. So he made it a matter of the ruling varying by the change of time and era, as they said regarding the issue of hiring for acts of obedience. Some gave a fatwa that if he pays the prompt and the deferred and is trustworthy, he may travel with her; otherwise not, because the deferment is established by custom; perhaps she only agreed to deferment for the sake of staying in her city. But if he takes her out to a foreign land, then no. The author of al-Majma' said in his commentary: and by this is the fatwa. So the fatwa differed, and the best is the fatwa according to the two fuqaha' without further detail, and it was chosen by many of the mashayikh as in al-Kafi, and upon it is the fatwa and the practice of judges in our time as in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. The author indicated by his saying 'and she has the right to prevent him' that she is an adult. If she is a minor, then the guardian has the mentioned prevention until he collects her mahr, and her handing over herself is not valid, so the guardian has the right to reclaim her. It is not for other than the father and the grandfather to hand her over to the husband before the one who has authority to collect the dowry receives it. If he hands her over, it is void, and she is returned to her house as in al-Tajnis and others.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding a husband's right to travel or move with his wife without her consent. The zahir al-riwayah (core transmitted ruling) from Imam Muhammad's six books states that the wife cannot refuse, based on the Quranic verse 'House them where you are housed' (65:6). However, later scholars like Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth gave fatwa that the husband may not force her due to the corruption of the times and the harm it causes to women. They refuted the objection that prioritizing the faqih's opinion over the Quran is wrong, by pointing out that the verse itself prohibits harm ('Do not harm them'). The passage cites many sources and concludes that the relied-upon fatwa is that the wife has the right to refuse. It also extends this to a minor wife, where her guardian can prevent the husband from taking her until the mahr is paid.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent (i.e., well-known) transmitted ruling from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
الإضرار (al-idrar): Causing harm or injury; the text uses it to argue that forcing travel is harmful to the wife.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The operative legal opinion given for practice; the text discusses differences in fatwa and settles on the more cautious view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa mentioned in this passage, what is the ruling on a husband traveling with his wife without her consent?
A) He has the right as long as he pays her prompt mahr.
B) He has the right if she gives her consent.
C) He can take her if he pays both prompt and deferred mahr.
D) He may not travel with her at all without her consent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa has evolved: a husband cannot force his wife to travel without her consent due to the principle of avoiding harm and changing times.

Dispute Over Mahr: When Husband and Wife Disagree
Ruling on mahr dispute with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling for a dispute over mahr amount, APPLY the mahr al-mithl benchmark to determine whose word is accepted, and EVALUATE the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute the mahr without evidence, the Hanafi school benchmarks mahr al-mithl to decide whose word holds.

Imagine a married couple disagrees on how much mahr was agreed upon, and neither has witnesses. How does a Hanafi qadi resolve this? This lesson from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling, the evidence from qiyas, and an important disagreement within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. You will learn how mahr al-mithl serves as a benchmark and how the concept of 'mustankir' (objectionably low) factors in.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The passage addresses when spouses differ on the mahr amount (e.g., husband says 1000, wife says 2000) without evidence. The ruling applies mahr al-mithl as a benchmark.
The benchmark is derived from women of similar status.
2
Apply the mahr al-mithl benchmark
Compare each party's claim to the mahr al-mithl. If mahr al-mithl is ≤ husband's claim, husband's word with oath; if ≥ wife's claim, wife's word with oath; if between, both take oaths.
The 'apparent' (zahir) supports the one whose claim aligns with mahr al-mithl.
3
Understand the role of nukul (refusal to swear)
If the party whose word is accepted refuses the oath (nukul), the opponent's claim becomes binding, either as admission or concession.
Nukul is treated as an implied admission.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf gives the husband's word unless the amount is 'mustankir' (objectionably low). The passage discusses its definition by custom vs. sharia (less than ten dirhams).
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Note the practical difference
Under Abu Yusuf, the husband wins unless his claim is absurdly low. Under the majority, mahr al-mithl is the decisive factor, potentially favoring the wife.
The thamarah al-khilaf is which party's word is accepted.

قوله : (وإن اختلفا في قدر المهر حكم مهر المثل أي اختلف الزوجان في قدره بأن وهي الفين وليس لأحدهما بينة فإنه يجعل مهر المثل حكماً، فإن كان مهر المثل ألفاً أو أقل فالقول قوله مع يمينه بالله ما تزوجتها على ألفين فإن حلف لزمه ما أقر به تسمية، وإن نكل لزمه ما ادعت المرأة على أنه مسمى لإقراره أو بذله بالنكول، وإن كان ألفين أو أكثر فالقول قولها مع اليمين بالله ما تزوجته بألف كما في الولوالجية، أو بالله ما رضيت بألف كما في شرح الطحاوي، فإن نكلت فلها ما أقر به الزوج تسمية لإقرارها به، وإن حلفت فلها جميع ما ادعت بقدر ما أقر به الزوج على أنه مسمى لاتفاقهما عليه، والزائد بحكم أنه مهر المثل لا باليمين حتى يتخير فيه الزوج بين الدراهم والدنانير. وإن مثلها أقل مما قالت وأكثر مما قال تحالفا وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه. وما وقع في النهاية من أن الزوج إذا نكل لزمه ألف وخمسمائة كأنه غلط من الناسخ، وإن وجب مهر المثل بقدر ما أقر به الزوج يجب على أنه مسمى والزائد بحكم مهر المثل حتى يتخير فيه بين دفع الدراهم والدنانير بخلاف الأول وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد أعني تحكيم مهر المثل وبناء الأمر عليه، وأبو يوسف لا يحكمه ويجعل القول قول الزوج مع يمينه إلا أن يأتي بشيء مستنكر لأن المرأة مدعية للزيادة وهو ينكرها. ولهما أن القول في الدعاوى قول من يشهد له الظاهر والظاهر شاهد لمن يشهد له مهر المثل لأنه هو الموجب الأصلي في باب النكاح وصار كالصباغ مع رب الثوب إذا اختلفا في مقدار الأجر تحكم قيمة الصبغ. واختلفا في تفسير المستنكر عنده فقيل هو المستنكر عرفاً ما لا يتعارف مهراً لها وصححه في الهداية والبدائع وشرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان، وذكر أنه وقيل هو المستنكر شرعاً وهو أن يدعي تزوجها على أقل من عشرة دراهم وهو مروي عنه في البدائع وصححه القاضي الأسبيجابي، وذكر الوبري أنه أشبه بالصواب لأنه ذكر في قول المصنف : (وإن اختلفا في قدر المهر) قال في الفتح: الاختلاف في المهر إما في قدره أو في أصله وكل منهما إما في حال الحياة أو بعد موتهما أو موت أحدهما، وكل منهما إما بعد الدخول أو قبله قوله : لزمه ما أقر به تسمية) أي لزمته الألف التي أقر بها على أنها تسمية فلا يتخير فيها بين أن يعطيها دراهم أو قيمتها ذهباً لأن الخيار يكون في الزائد دون المسمى قوله : (الاقراره أو بذله بالنكول) علة لقوله «الزمه» أي لزمه ما ادعته لأن النكول إقرار أو بذل على الخلاف قوله : (بخلاف الأول أي قدر ما أقر به الزوج فإنه لا يتخير فيه لأنه
His saying: 'And if they differ regarding the amount of the mahr, the mahr of the like is judged' – meaning the spouses differed regarding its amount, e.g., he said one thousand and she said two thousand, and neither has evidence. Then the mahr of the like is made the ruling. If the mahr of the like is one thousand or less, then the word is his with an oath by Allah that he did not marry her for two thousand. If he swears, what he admits becomes binding as specified (musamma). If he refuses (nukul), what the woman claimed becomes binding as specified due to his admission or his concession by nukul. If it is two thousand or more, then the word is hers with an oath by Allah that he did not marry her for one thousand, as in al-Walwaljiya, or by Allah that she was not satisfied with a thousand as in Sharh al-Tahawi. If she refuses, she gets what the husband admitted as specified due to her admission. If she swears, she gets all that she claimed by the amount the husband admitted as specified due to their agreement, and the excess by the ruling that it is mahr al-mithl, not by the oath, so the husband may choose between dirhams and dinars for the excess. If her mahr al-mithl is less than what she said and more than what he said, they both take oaths, and whichever refuses, the claim of the other becomes binding. What occurred in al-Nihaya that if the husband refuses, one thousand five hundred becomes binding – this seems to be an error by the copyist. If mahr al-mithl is due to the amount that the husband admitted, it is due as specified, and the excess is by the ruling of mahr al-mithl, so he may choose between paying dirhams and dinars, unlike the first case. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, i.e., applying mahr al-mithl and building the matter upon it. Abu Yusuf does not apply it and gives the word to the husband with his oath unless he comes with something objectionable (mustankir), because the woman is claiming an increase and he denies it. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the word in claims is for the one supported by the apparent, and the apparent supports the one supported by mahr al-mithl because it is the original obligation in marriage, and it is like the dyer with the owner of the cloth: if they differ on the amount of the fee, the value of the dye is judged. They differed on the interpretation of 'mustankir' according to him. It is said: 'mustankir' according to custom is what is not customarily a dower for her, and he corrected it in al-Hidaya, al-Bada'i', and Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadi Khan. And it is said: 'mustankir' according to sharia is claiming marriage for less than ten dirhams, and it is narrated from him in al-Bada'i', and al-Qadi al-Asbijabi corrected it. Al-Wabri mentioned that it is closer to correctness because he mentioned in the saying of the author: 'And if they differ regarding the amount of the mahr.' He said in al-Fath: the difference in mahr is either in its amount or in its origin, and each of them is either during life or after their death or the death of one of them, and each of them is either after consummation or before. His saying: 'what he admitted becomes binding as specified' means the thousand he admitted becomes binding as a specified dower, so he cannot choose between giving dirhams or its value in gold, because choice is in the excess, not in the specified. His saying: 'due to his admission or his concession by nukul' is the cause for his saying 'becomes binding' – i.e., what she claimed becomes binding because nukul is either an admission or a concession according to the difference. His saying: 'unlike the first case' means the amount that the husband admitted: he does not have choice in it because...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling when spouses disagree on the amount of mahr after marriage, with no evidence. The commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: they refer to mahr al-mithl (the dower of women of similar status). If the mahr al-mithl is equal to or less than what the husband claims, his word with oath is accepted; if it is equal to or greater than what the wife claims, her word with oath is accepted. If the mahr al-mithl falls between their claims, both take oaths and the one who refuses loses. The passage also discusses Abu Yusuf's dissenting opinion, which gives the husband the word unless the amount is 'mustankir' (objectionably low), and the different interpretations of 'mustankir' (customarily vs. shari'ah low, the latter being less than ten dirhams). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it is from the zahir al-riwayah. The commentary also clarifies that the specified mahr (musamma) is binding as admitted, while any excess over that is considered mahr al-mithl, allowing the husband to choose between paying in dirhams or dinars.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower that is customary for women of similar status to the bride (in terms of family, beauty, wealth, etc.).
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal to take an oath when required; the text treats nukul as equivalent to an admission or concession of the opponent's claim.
المستنكر (al-mustankir): An objectionably low amount of mahr; Abu Yusuf gives the husband the word unless his claim is mustankir. The text discusses whether it is defined by custom or by sharia (less than ten dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if spouses dispute the mahr amount and the wife's mahr al-mithl is one thousand dirhams (the wife claims two thousand, the husband claims five hundred), whose word is accepted?
A) The husband's word with oath.
B) The wife's word with oath.
C) Both must swear, and the one who refuses loses.
D) The mahr al-mithl is imposed directly.

Key Takeaway
In a mahr dispute without evidence, the Hanafi school benchmarks mahr al-mithl to decide whose word is accepted, with the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) as the mufta bihi.

Adjudicating Mahr Disputes: Mahr al-Mithl and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Expansion of a matn ruling on mahr disputes with proof and intra-madhhab difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of mahr al-mithl when spouses dispute the dower amount without evidence, explain the Hanafi qiyas with the dyer, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute mahr without proof, the court adjudicates the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) as the standard.

A common family dispute arises when a husband and wife disagree on the agreed dower amount, and neither can produce witnesses. Islamic courts rely on a systematic procedure to resolve such conflicts. This lesson explores the Hanafi approach: applying mahr al-mithl (proper dower) as the benchmark, a method derived by analogy to commercial disputes, and the internal difference with Abu Yusuf on when to accept the husband's word.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
We are given a case where the spouses disagree on the mahr amount (e.g., husband says 1000, wife says 2000) and neither has evidence. The first analytical step is to recognize the absence of proof and the need for a default standard.
The text explicitly excludes cases where evidence exists; those are decided by the one who proves.
2
State the primary Hanafi ruling
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the court determines the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) and then accepts the statement of the spouse whose claim aligns with that value, with an oath. If the proper dower is between their claims, both must take oaths (tahaluf).
This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogical proof)
The ruling is analogized to a dispute between a dyer and garment owner over the fee: the court adjudicates the market value of the dye. Similarly, the proper dower (value of marital submission) is the standard. Identify the asl (dyer case), far' (mahr dispute), illah (common need for a value when evidence fails), and hukm (adjudicate proper value).
The illah is extracted by tahqiq al-manat: the value of the service is the objective standard.
4
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf does not apply mahr al-mithl automatically. He accepts the husband's statement with oath unless the husband claims an outrageously low amount (mustankar). The wife is the claimant; the default is defendant's word. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
Mustankar is defined either customarily (what is not customary for that woman) or legally (less than 10 dirhams).
5
Note the later procedural development on tahaluf
Later Hanafi scholars differed on when mutual oaths (tahaluf) are required. Al-Razi held it applies only when the proper dower differs from both claims; al-Karkhi held it applies in all three scenarios. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is al-Karkhi's, as cited in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit.
Also, the question of who begins the oath: some say the husband, others recommend a lottery (qur'ah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

إلى بيتها كما في التجنيس وغيره. قوله : (وإن اختلفا في قدر المهر حكم مهر المثل) أي اختلف الزوجان في قدره بأن وهي الفين وليس لأحدهما بينة فإنه يجعل مهر المثل حكماً، فإن كان مهر المثل ألفاً أو أقل فالقول قوله مع يمينه بالله ما تزوجتها على ألفين فإن حلف لزمه ما أقر به تسمية، وإن نكل لزمه ما ادعت المرأة على أنه مسمى لإقراره أو بذله بالنكول، وإن كان ألفين أو أكثر فالقول قولها مع اليمين بالله ما تزوجته بحكم أنه مهر المثل لا باليمين حتى يتخير فيه الزوج بين الدراهم والدنانير. وإن مثلها أقل مما قالت وأكثر مما قال تحالفا وأيهما نكل لزمه دعوى صاحبه. وما وقع في النهاية من أن الزوج إذا نكل لزمه ألف وخمسمائة كأنه غلط من الناسخ، وإن وجب مهر المثل بقدر ما أقر به الزوج يجب على أنه مسمى والزائد بحكم مهر المثل حتى يتخير فيه بين دفع الدراهم والدنانير بخلاف الأول وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد أعني تحكيم مهر المثل وبناء الأمر عليه، وأبو يوسف لا يحكمه ويجعل القول قول الزوج مع يمينه إلا أن يأتي بشيء مستنكر لأن المرأة مدعية للزيادة وهو ينكرها. ولهما أن القول في الدعاوى قول من يشهد له الظاهر والظاهر شاهد لمن يشهد له مهر المثل لأنه هو الموجب الأصلي في باب النكاح وصار كالصباغ مع رب الثوب إذا اختلفا في مقدار الأجر تحكم قيمة الصبغ. واختلفا في تفسير المستنكر عنده فقيل هو المستنكر عرفاً ما لا يتعارف مهراً لها وصححه في الهداية والبدائع وشرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان، وذكر أنه وقيل هو المستنكر شرعاً وهو أن يدعي تزوجها على أقل من عشرة دراهم وهو مروي عنه في البدائع وصححه القاضي الأسبيجابي، وذكر الوبري أنه أشبه بالصواب لأنه ذكر في حلفا كما مهر مروي عنه، يعرفها واستمرت مدة عند من اشتراها حتى سمع بذلك أهلها فأخرجوا أمراً من جانب السلطنة العلية بأخذها فأخذت ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله قول المصنف : (وإن اختلفا في قدر المهر) قال في الفتح: الاختلاف في المهر إما في قدره أو في أصله وكل منهما إما في حال الحياة أو بعد موتهما أو موت أحدهما، وكل منهما إما بعد الدخول أو قبله قوله : لزمه ما أقر به تسمية) أي لزمته الألف التي أقر بها على أنها تسمية فلا يتخير فيها بين أن يعطيها دراهم أو قيمتها ذهباً لأن الخيار يكون في الزائد دون المسمى قوله : (الاقراره أو بذله بالنكول) علة لقوله «الزمه» أي لزمه ما ادعته لأن النكول إقرار أو بذل على الخلاف قوله : (بخلاف الأول أي قدر ما أقر به الزوج فإنه لا يتخير فيه لأنه كتاب النكاح باب المهر ٣١٥ كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة لو ادعى أنه تزوجها على مائة وهي تدعي أنه تزوجها على ألف ومهر مثلها ألف وأقام البينة ثم رجع الشهود لا يضمنون عند أبي يوسف لأنه لولا الشهادة كان القول قوله ولم يجعل المائة مستنكراً في حقها، واختاره في فتح القدير. وعبارة الجامع الصغير: إلا أن يأتي بشيء قليل. وفي غاية البيان ولفظ الجامع الصغير أبين اهـ. مع أن الاحتمال موجود فيها أيضاً لأنه يحتمل أن يكون المراد بالقليل ما قل شرعاً أو عرفاً فساوت التعبير بالمستنكر المذكور في غيره وظاهر كلام المصنف هنا أن تحكيم مهر المثل معتبر قبل التحالف وهو مبني على تخريج أبي بكر الرازي، وحاصله أن التحالف على تخريجه في فصل واحد وهو ما إذا خالف مهر المثل قولهما وأما إذا وافق قول أحدهما فالقول قوله وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير لأنه لا حاجة إليه مع شهادة الظاهر وذكر المصنف في باب التحالف من كتاب الدعوى أنهما يتحالفان ثم يحكم مهر المثل وهو على تخريج الكرخي وصححه في المبسوط والمحيط وحاصله وجوب التحالف في الفصول الثلاثة أعني ما إذا وافق مهر المثل قوله أو قولها أو خالفهما، فإذا تحالفا قضى بقوله لو كان مهر المثل كما قال، وبقولها لو كان كما قالت وبمهر المثل لو كان بينهما لأن مهر المثل لا يصار إليه إلا عند سقوط التسمية وهي لا تسقط إلا بالتحالف، والظاهر لا يكون حجة على الغير، ولم أر من صحح تخريج الرازي فكان المذهب تخريج الكرخي، فيحمل كلام المصنف هنا عليه ليطابق ما صرح به في بابه. ولم يذكر المصنف في الموضعين بمن يبدأ في التحالف للاختلاف فذكر في غاية البيان أنه يقرع بينهما يعني استحباباً لأنه لا رجحان لأحدهما على الآخر. واختار في الظهيرية والولوالجية وشرح الطحاوي وكثير أنه يبدأ بيمين الزوج لأن أول التسليمين عليه فيكون أول اليمينين عليه كتقديم المشتري على البائع في التحالف. والخلاف في الأولوية حتى لو بدأ بأيهما كان جائزاً كما في فتح القدير. وقيدنا بعدم إقامة البينة لأنه لو قامت لأحدهما بينة قضى ببيئته، وإنما سكت عنه المصنف هنا لأنه صرح به في بابه وعبارته : وإن اختلفا في المهر قضى لمن برهن وإن برهنا فللمرأة، وإن عجزا تحالفا إلى آخره إلا أن قوله «وإن برهنا فللمرأة شامل لما إذا كان مهر المثل شاهداً له أو لها أو بينهما، وفي الأول البيئة بينتها لأنها تثبت أمراً زائداً، وأما في الثاني ففيه اختلاف ذكره في البدائع. قال وجب على أنه مسمى قوله : (ولم أر من صحح تخريج الرازي قال في النهر أقول: تقديم الشارح وغيره تبعاً لصاحب الهداية ماخرجه الرازي يؤذن بترجيحه وصححه في النهاية. وقال قاضيخان : إنه الأولى. واختيار المصنف له هنا لا ينافي اختيار غيره في موضع آخر وحمل كلامه هنا على ما قاله في التحالف ظاهر البعد إذ وجوب المسألة حينئذ تخالفا وحكم مهر المثل ولا دلالة. في كلامه على هذا المحذوف قوله : (لأن أول التسليمين (عليه قال الرملي : أي تسليم المهر ثم تسليم نفعها
If he claimed a thousand while she was a minor, then the guardian has the mentioned prohibition until he receives her dower, and her handing over herself is not valid, so the guardian can reclaim her. And it is not for anyone other than the father and grandfather to hand her over to the husband before the one who has authority to receive the dower has received it. If he hands her over, it is invalid and she is returned to her house as in al-Tajnīs and other works. His statement: (And if they differ over the amount of the dower, the proper dower is judged) i.e., the two spouses differed over its amount, for example he said one thousand and she said two thousand, and neither has evidence, then the proper dower is made the ruling. If the proper dower is one thousand or less, his statement is accepted with his oath, 'By Allah, I did not marry her for two thousand.' If he swears, he is liable for what he acknowledged as specified (tasmīyah). If he refuses (nakala), he is liable for what the woman claimed as specified, due to his acknowledgment or his surrender by refusal. If it is two thousand or more, her statement is accepted with the oath, 'By Allah, he did not marry me for one thousand' as in al-Walwālijiyyah, or 'By Allah, I was not satisfied with one thousand' as in Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī. If she refuses, she gets what the husband acknowledged as specified due to her acknowledgment. If she swears, she gets all that she claimed to the extent of what the husband acknowledged as specified due to their agreement on it, and the excess is by virtue of proper dower, not by oath, so the husband may choose between dirhams and dinars for it. If her proper dower is less than what she said and more than what he said, they both take oaths, and whichever refuses is liable for the other's claim. What occurs in al-Nihāyah that if the husband refuses he is liable for one thousand five hundred seems to be a scribal error. If the proper dower is obligatory to the extent of what the husband acknowledged, it is obligatory as specified, and the excess is by virtue of proper dower, so he may choose between paying dirhams and dinars, unlike the first case. This is the statement of Abū Ḥanīfah and Muḥammad, i.e., applying the proper dower and building the matter upon it. Abū Yūsuf does not apply it and makes the husband's statement accepted with his oath unless he brings something outrageous (mustankar), because the woman is claiming an increase and he denies it. Their evidence is that in claims, the statement is of the one supported by the apparent (ẓāhir), and the apparent supports the proper dower because it is the original obligator in marriage, and it becomes like the dyer with the garment owner when they differ over the amount of the fee, the value of the dye is adjudicated. They differed over the interpretation of 'outrageous' according to him. It is said it is what is outrageous customarily, i.e., what is not customary as a dower for her, and this was deemed correct in al-Hidāyah, al-Badā'iʿ, and Sharḥ al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr by Qāḍīkhān. And it is mentioned that it is said it is what is outrageous legally, i.e., he claims he married her for less than ten dirhams, and this is narrated from him in al-Badā'iʿ and deemed correct by al-Qāḍī al-Asbījābī. Al-Wabirī mentioned that it is more correct because it is mentioned in... [text continues]
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from Baḥr al-Rāʾiq is a commentary expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq regarding disputes over the amount of mahr (dower) in a marriage contract. The author first discusses a scenario where the wife is a minor and the guardian has the right to prevent her from being handed over until he receives the dower. He then moves to the core issue: when the spouses differ on the amount of mahr and neither has evidence. The ruling is that the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is applied as a standard, analogous to the case of a dyer and a garment owner differing over the fee. This is the position of Abū Ḥanīfah and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī: the court looks to the proper dower as the original obligation in marriage. If the proper dower aligns with the husband's claim, his statement is accepted with oath; if with the wife's, hers is accepted. Abū Yūsuf disagrees: he does not apply the proper dower but rather accepts the husband's statement with oath unless the husband claims an outrageously low amount (mustankar). The disputants differ on the definition of 'mustankar': some define it customarily (what is not customary for that woman), others legally (less than ten dirhams). The author then discusses the procedure of mutual oaths (taḥāluf) when the proper dower does not align with either claim. The commentary by al-Karkhī and al-Rāzī on when taḥāluf is required is presented; the author leans toward al-Karkhī's position that taḥāluf is mandatory in all cases. Finally, he discusses who begins the oath: some say the husband because he is the first to submit the mahr; others suggest a lottery. The overall lesson is a detailed, practical guide for a qāḍī (judge) in adjudicating mahr disputes.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the court based on the dower of women similar to the wife in social status, family, etc.
مستنكر (mustankar): An outrageously low or high dower that is not customary or legal. It triggers different procedures.
تحالف (taḥāluf): Mutual oath-taking by both spouses when they disagree on the mahr amount and neither has evidence, leading to a ruling based on oaths.
نكول (nukūl): Refusal to take an oath after being required to do so; considered acknowledgment of the opponent's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the position of Abū Yūsuf regarding the dispute over mahr amount when the husband's claim is not outrageously low?
A) He applies mahr al-mithl and decides accordingly.
B) He accepts the wife's statement with her oath.
C) He accepts the husband's statement with his oath.
D) He requires both spouses to take oaths (taḥāluf) first.

Key Takeaway
When spouses dispute the mahr amount without evidence, the Hanafi school adjudicates mahr al-mithl as the standard, based on qiyas with the dyer, though Abu Yusuf prefers accepting the husband's word unless the claim is outrageous.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses in Mahr Disputes
Explains the ruling when witnesses retract in a mahr dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retracting witnesses in a mahr dispute and explain the reasoning based on default plausibility and the concept of mustankar.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract are not liable if their testimony did not change the default legal position.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Hanafi fiqh: when witnesses testify in a mahr dispute and then retract. The key question is whether they must compensate the husband for his loss. Abu Yusuf's ruling establishes an important principle about the burden of proof and the concept of mustankar (improbable). We will walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
The husband claims the mahr was 100, the wife claims 1,000, and her mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) is 1,000. The husband brings witnesses who testify for him, then they retract.
Mahr al-mithl is used as a benchmark to assess plausibility.
2
Determine the default legal position
Without any testimony, the husband's claim would be accepted. In Hanafi law, when the husband admits marriage but disputes the amount, his statement is taken as true because he is the one acknowledging the marriage (burden of proof shifts to the one claiming more).
Default: husband's claim of 100 stands.
3
Analyze the impact of the testimony
The witnesses testified for the husband. If they had not, the husband would have won by default. Thus, their testimony did not alter the outcome; it only confirmed what was already the legal default.
No harm caused by the testimony; retraction does not create new liability.
4
Apply the concept of mustankar
The husband's claim of 100 is not considered mustankar (improbable/outrageous) because a low mahr is possible by custom or Shariah, even if the wife's mahr al-mithl is 1,000. Therefore, the testimony did not contradict a clearly improbable claim.
If the claim were mustankar, the default might shift.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since the testimony did not change the default and the claim was not mustankar, the retracting witnesses are not liable. This is the position of Abu Yusuf, chosen in Fath al-Qadir.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists; other views may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادة لو ادعى أنه تزوجها على مائة وهي تدعي أنه تزوجها على ألف ومهر مثلها ألف وأقام البينة ثم رجع الشهود لا يضمنون عند أبي يوسف لأنه لولا الشهادة كان القول قوله ولم يجعل المائة مستنكراً في حقها، واختاره في فتح القدير. وعبارة الجامع الصغير: إلا أن يأتي بشيء قليل. وفي غاية البيان ولفظ الجامع الصغير أبين اهـ. مع أن الاحتمال موجود فيها أيضاً لأنه يحتمل أن يكون المراد بالقليل ما قل شرعاً أو عرفاً فساوت التعبير بالمستنكر المذكور في غيره
Book of Retraction of Testimony: If a man claims he married her for a hundred and she claims he married her for a thousand, and her mahr al-mithl is a thousand, and he brings witnesses, then the witnesses retract: they are not liable according to Abu Yusuf, because without the testimony, the statement would be his, and he did not consider the hundred to be improbable regarding her. And he (the author of Fath al-Qadir) chose it. The expression in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Unless he brings something small.' And in Ghayat al-Bayan: the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir is clearer. Although the possibility exists in it as well, because it is possible that by 'small' is meant what is small according to Shariah or custom, so it is equivalent to the expression 'improbable' mentioned elsewhere.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when witnesses retract their testimony in a mahr dispute. The case: husband claims mahr is 100, wife claims 1,000, and her proper mahr (mahr al-mithl) is 1,000. Husband brings witnesses who testify for him (that mahr is 100), then they retract. According to Abu Yusuf, they are not liable to indemnify the husband. The reason: without the testimony, the husband's claim would have been accepted (since he admits the marriage and she claims more). The witnesses' testimony did not contradict what was already plausible; 100 is not 'mustankar' (unlikely/outrageous) from her perspective because mahr al-mithl is 1,000, so 100 is low but not impossible. Thus, the witnesses are not liable. The author of Fath al-Qadir chose this view. The passage then compares the phrasing in al-Jami' al-Saghir which uses 'something small' (shay' qalil), explaining that this is equivalent to 'mustankar' in meaning.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah): The act of a witness withdrawing his testimony after having given it.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper or standard mahr for a woman of similar status in her family.
مستنكر (mustankar): Considered improbable or outlandish given the circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case discussed, why are the retracting witnesses not liable according to Abu Yusuf?
A) Because the wife failed to prove her claim
B) Because without the testimony, the husband's statement would have been accepted
C) Because the witnesses were coerced
D) Because the mahr al-mithl is higher than both claims

Key Takeaway
Retracting witnesses are not liable if their testimony merely confirmed a default legal position and the claim was not improbable (mustankar).

Two Derivation Approaches on Tahaluf and Mahr al-Mithl
Presents two scholarly approaches regarding the role of mahr al-mithl before mutual oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare Abu Bakr al-Razi's and al-Karkhi's derivations on the role of mahr al-mithl before mutual oath, apply al-Karkhi's view to determine the procedural steps, and state the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Mutual oath is obligatory before resorting to mahr al-mithl; external evidence cannot override a specified mahr without the parties' oaths.

In this lesson, you will explore an intra-Hanafi debate: when a husband and wife dispute the mahr amount and the mahr al-mithl is known, should the judge require mutual oath (tahaluf) before imposing the mahr al-mithl? Abu Bakr al-Razi and al-Karkhi offered two different derivations (takhrij). Understanding their reasoning and the school's choice is key to applying the correct procedure in such disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two derivations and their proponents
First, recognise that al-Razi and al-Karkhi are both Hanafi scholars who derived different rules from the same principles. al-Razi's derivation is associated with the statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir, while al-Karkhi's is upheld in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit.
Both are legitimate extensions of Hanafi usul; the dispute is purely methodological.
2
Analyze al-Razi's scenario breakdown
Under al-Razi, mutual oath is only required when the mahr al-mithl contradicts both claims. If it agrees with one party, that party's claim is accepted without oath because the mahr al-mithl serves as external evidence (shahadat al-zahir).
This view reduces the number of cases requiring oath.
3
Analyze al-Karkhi's scenario breakdown
Under al-Karkhi, mutual oath is obligatory in all three scenarios: when mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, agrees with the wife, or contradicts both. After oath, the ruling follows the claim that matches the mahr al-mithl, or the mahr al-mithl itself if it lies between the two claims.
The rationale: the specified mahr is only dropped by mutual oath; external evidence is not a proof against the parties.
4
Understand the key principle driving al-Karkhi's view
Al-Karkhi's derivation rests on the principle that a validly specified mahr remains binding until it is invalidated by the parties' own statements under oath. The mahr al-mithl is a fallback that cannot preempt the specified mahr.
This aligns with the general Hanafi preference for upholding contractual terms.
5
Determine the relied-upon position and the reason
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq states that he has not seen anyone correct al-Razi's derivation, so the madhhab is al-Karkhi's. Thus, the mufta bihi position is that mutual oath is always required before mahr al-mithl can be considered.
This is also consistent with the author's own chapter on tahaluf in the Book of Claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاهر كلام المصنف هنا أن تحكيم مهر المثل معتبر قبل التحالف وهو مبني على تخريج أبي بكر الرازي، وحاصله أن التحالف على تخريجه في فصل واحد وهو ما إذا خالف مهر المثل قولهما وأما إذا وافق قول أحدهما فالقول قوله وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير لأنه لا حاجة إليه مع شهادة الظاهر وذكر المصنف في باب التحالف من كتاب الدعوى أنهما يتحالفان ثم يحكم مهر المثل وهو على تخريج الكرخي وصححه في المبسوط والمحيط وحاصله وجوب التحالف في الفصول الثلاثة أعني ما إذا وافق مهر المثل قوله أو قولها أو خالفهما، فإذا تحالفا قضى بقوله لو كان مهر المثل كما قال، وبقولها لو كان كما قالت وبمهر المثل لو كان بينهما لأن مهر المثل لا يصار إليه إلا عند سقوط التسمية وهي لا تسقط إلا بالتحالف، والظاهر لا يكون حجة على الغير، ولم أر من صحح تخريج الرازي فكان المذهب تخريج الكرخي، فيحمل كلام المصنف هنا عليه ليطابق ما صرح به في بابه.
The apparent meaning of the author's words here is that the determination of mahr al-mithl is considered before mutual oath, and this is based on the derivation of Abu Bakr al-Razi. Its summary is that according to his derivation, mutual oath occurs in one scenario only: when the mahr al-mithl contradicts both their statements. As for when it agrees with one of their statements, that statement is taken, and this is what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, because there is no need for mutual oath when external evidence (the mahr al-mithl) supports it. The author mentioned in the chapter of mutual oath in the Book of Claims that they take mutual oaths and then mahr al-mithl is adjudged, and this is based on the derivation of al-Karkhi, which he corrected in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit. Its summary is the obligation of mutual oath in all three scenarios: when the mahr al-mithl agrees with his statement, agrees with her statement, or contradicts both. When they take mutual oaths, judgment is given according to his statement if the mahr al-mithl is as he said, according to her statement if it is as she said, and by mahr al-mithl if it is between them, because mahr al-mithl is only resorted to when the specified mahr is dropped, and it is only dropped by mutual oath, and external evidence (mahr al-mithl) is not a proof against others. I have not seen anyone correct the derivation of al-Razi, so the madhhab is the derivation of al-Karkhi. Therefore, the author's words here are interpreted according to it to match what he clarified in its chapter.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents two competing derivations (takhrij) within the Hanafi school regarding the role of mahr al-mithl in a mahr dispute. The issue: When the husband and wife disagree on the mahr amount, and the mahr al-mithl is known, should mutual oath (tahaluf) be required before referring to mahr al-mithl? Abu Bakr al-Razi's derivation: Mutual oath is only needed when the mahr al-mithl contradicts both claims. If it agrees with one, that claim is accepted without oath because the mahr al-mithl serves as external evidence. Al-Karkhi's derivation: Mutual oath is obligatory in all three cases (mahr al-mithl agrees with husband, with wife, or between them). After oath, the ruling follows the one whose claim matches the mahr al-mithl, or if between them, mahr al-mithl is imposed. The reason: the specified mahr is only dropped via mutual oath; mahr al-mithl cannot override a valid claim. The author states that the relied-upon position is al-Karkhi's, as al-Razi's derivation was not corrected by later scholars. Thus, the author's statement here is interpreted to align with al-Karkhi's view for consistency with his own chapter on mutual oath.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): A derivation or extension of a ruling from foundational principles to a new case.
التحالف (al-tahāluf): The mutual taking of oaths by two disputing parties when each swears to his or her claim.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard mahr determined by the mahr of female relatives of similar status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only when mahr al-mithl contradicts both claims
B) Only when mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband's claim
C) In all three scenarios: when mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, with the wife, or contradicts both
D) Never; the court decides based on mahr al-mithl without oath

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that mutual oath is always required in mahr disputes before mahr al-mithl can be applied; the specified mahr is only dropped by oath.

Who Begins the Oath in Tahaluf?
Discusses who begins the mutual oath and the recommended practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred party to initiate the oath in tahaluf and explain the basis of the difference of opinion.

Core Idea
Preference for the husband to begin the oath in tahaluf is based on analogy to the buyer's precedence in sale disputes.

In a dispute over mahr where both parties claim and lack evidence, the judge may order a mutual oath (tahaluf). A procedural question arises: who begins? The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not specify, leading to scholarly discussion. This lesson examines the recommended practice and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that tahaluf occurs in a mahr dispute when both parties have no evidence. The judge orders both to swear oaths.
Tahaluf is a procedure to resolve conflicting claims.
2
State the first opinion
Some Hanafi sources (e.g., Ghayat al-Bayan) recommend drawing lots (qur'ah) to determine who swears first, as there is no inherent preference.
This is considered a recommendation (istihbab), not an obligation.
3
State the second opinion
Other authorities (al-Zahiriyyah, al-Walwaljiyyah, Sharh al-Tahawi, and many) prefer that the husband swears first.
This view is chosen by many later Hanafi scholars.
4
Understand the reasoning
The husband's precedence is analogized to the buyer in a sale dispute: the buyer pays first, so he swears first. Similarly, the husband is obligated to pay the mahr, so he should begin the oath.
The analogy is qiyas on the ruling of tahaluf in sales.
5
Recognize the nature of the difference
The disagreement is over preference (awlawiyyah), not obligation. Either party may begin; the recommended practice is for the husband.
As stated in Fath al-Qadir, it is permissible regardless of who begins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف في الموضعين بمن يبدأ في التحالف للاختلاف فذكر في غاية البيان أنه يقرع بينهما يعني استحباباً لأنه لا رجحان لأحدهما على الآخر. واختار في الظهيرية والولوالجية وشرح الطحاوي وكثير أنه يبدأ بيمين الزوج لأن أول التسليمين عليه فيكون أول اليمينين عليه كتقديم المشتري على البائع في التحالف. والخلاف في الأولوية حتى لو بدأ بأيهما كان جائزاً كما في فتح القدير.
The author did not mention in either place who begins the mutual oath due to disagreement. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that lots are cast between them, meaning as a recommendation, because there is no preference of one over the other. And in al-Zahiriyyah, al-Walwaljiyyah, Sharh al-Tahawi, and many others, they chose that the husband begins the oath, because the first of two obligations is upon him, so the first of two oaths is upon him, like the preference of the buyer over the seller in mutual oath. The difference is one of preference; even if either one begins, it is permissible, as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage addresses the procedural question in a mahr dispute: which party should take the first oath in tahaluf? The author (of Kanz al-Daqaiq) did not specify, so the commentator discusses the differing opinions. One view (in Ghayat al-Bayan) recommends drawing lots (qur'ah) since there is no inherent preference. Another view, chosen by multiple authorities (al-Zahiriyyah, al-Walwaljiyyah, Sharh al-Tahawi, and others), holds that the husband should begin. Their reasoning: just as the husband is obligated to pay the mahr first (before the wife's obligation to submit), he should also take the first oath. This is analogous to mutual oath in a sale dispute where the buyer (who pays) swears first. However, this is a matter of preference (first olawiyyah), not obligation. It is permissible for either party to begin, as confirmed in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
القرعة (al-qur'ah): Drawing lots to determine who begins the oath, as a recommended method.
الأولوية (al-awlawiyyah): Preference or superiority; here, who should preferably begin the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view chosen in al-Zahiriyyah and others, who starts the oath in tahaluf and why?
A) The wife, because she is the one claiming a larger mahr
B) The husband, because the first of two obligations (the mahr) is upon him
C) A judge decides by drawing lots
D) The parties take the oath simultaneously

Key Takeaway
The husband is preferred to initiate tahaluf in mahr disputes by analogy to the buyer's oath in sale, but either party may begin.

Conflicting Evidence in Mahr: Neutralization and Ikhtilaf
Explains the ruling when both husband and wife present evidence in a mahr dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when both husband and wife present evidence on the mahr amount, distinguishing the three scenarios based on mahr al-mithl, and identify the ikhtilaf regarding whose evidence prevails.

Core Idea
When both parties present evidence, mahr al-mithl determines who wins—unless it's between them, then evidences cancel and full mahr al-mithl is due.

This lesson addresses a nuanced situation in mahr disputes: both spouses claim different amounts and each brings witnesses. The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) gives a general rule favoring the wife, but the commentator unpacks three distinct sub-cases relative to mahr al-mithl. Inside these sub-cases lies an intra-Hanafi disagreement, a comparison with sale, and the principle of tahātur (neutralization).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
First, classify the case based on how mahr al-mithl relates to the conflicting claims: (1) mahr al-mithl supports the husband's claim, (2) mahr al-mithl supports the wife's claim, (3) mahr al-mithl lies between both claims.
This classification is the key to understanding the different rulings.
2
Analyze scenario 1 (mahr al-mithl supports husband)
Even though mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife's evidence prevails because it proves an additional amount beyond what the mahr al-mithl shows. Her evidence introduces new information.
Here, the wife's evidence is considered 'zā'id' (additional), so it outweighs.
3
Analyze scenario 2 (mahr al-mithl supports wife) – the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute. One view (al-Zayla'i) favors the husband because his evidence shows a reduction from the mahr al-mithl, while the wife's evidence adds nothing new. Another view favors the wife because mahr al-mithl is not proof against third parties, so her evidence brings new information.
This disagreement hinges on whether mahr al-mithl is considered 'evidence' against the parties.
4
Determine the ruling in scenario 3 (mahr al-mithl between both claims)
When mahr al-mithl falls between the claims, the two pieces of evidence neutralize (tahātur) because they are equally strong. Then the full mahr al-mithl is due, and the husband may choose currency.
This is different from tahāluf (mutual oath), where only the agreed portion is specified.
5
Distinguish from the sale analogy
The passage includes a statement from Muhammad al-Shaybani contrasting marriage with sale: in sale, both evidences can be reconciled by assuming two separate contracts (since sale can be rescinded), but marriage cannot be rescinded, so the evidences cancel.
This highlights the special nature of nikah – it is not easily dissolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أن قوله «وإن برهنا فللمرأة» شامل لما إذا كان مهر المثل شاهداً له أو لها أو بينهما، وفي الأول البيئة بينتها لأنها تثبت أمراً زائداً، وأما في الثاني ففيه اختلاف ذكره في البدائع. قال وجب على أنه مسمى قوله : (ولم أر من صحح تخريج الرازي قال في النهر أقول: تقديم الشارح وغيره تبعاً لصاحب الهداية ماخرجه الرازي يؤذن بترجيحه وصححه في النهاية. وقال قاضيخان : إنه الأولى. واختيار المصنف له هنا لا ينافي تسليم المهر ثم تسليم نفعها بعضهم : يقضى ببينتها أيضاً لأنها أظهرت شيئاً لم يكن ظاهراً بتصادقهما، وأما الظهور بشهادة مهر المثل فلا اعتبار به لما قدمنا أنه لا يكون حجة على الغير وقال بعضهم : يقضى ببيئة الزوج بينته تظهر حط الألف عن مهر المثل وبينتها لا تظهر شيئاً لأن الألفين كانت ظاهرة بشهادة مهر المثل، وهذا القول جزم به الزيلعي في باب التحالف وفي هذا الموضع . وأما في الثالث وهو ما إذا كان بينهما فالصحيح أنهما يتهاتران لاستوائهما في الدعوى والإثبات ثم يجب مهر المثل كله فيتخير فيه الزوج بين دفع الدراهم والدنانير بخلاف التحالف لأن بينة كل واحد منهما تنفي تسمية صاحبه فخلا العقد عن التسمية فيجب مهر المثل ولا كذلك التحالف لأن وجوب قدر ما يقربه الزوج بحكم الاتفاق والزائد بحكم مهر المثل هكذا ذكره الكرماتي. وذكر قاضيخان أنه يجب قدر ما اتفقا عليه على أنه مسمى والزائد على أنه مهر المثل كما في التحالف، والظاهر الأول كما لا يخفى. وفي المحيط وقال محمد : رجل أقام بينة على أنه تزوج هذه المرأة بألف وأقامت بينة أنه تزوجها على ألفين فالمهر ألف ولو أقام رجل بينة أنه اشترى هذه الدار بألف وأقام البائع بينة أنه باعها منه بألفين فهي بألفين والفرق أن في البيع أمكن العمل بالبيتنين لاحتمال أنه اشترى منه أولاً ثم اشتراها منه بألفين ثانياً كما سيأتي فيصح، لأن البيع يحتمل الفسخ والنكاح لا يحتمل الفسخ وكل منهما ادعى عقداً غير ما ادعاه الآخر فتهاترت البينتان ووجب لها الألف باعتراف الزوج .اهـ.
We restricted [the previous discussion] to the case of no evidence, because if one of them establishes evidence, judgment is given by his evidence. The author omitted this here because he clarified it in its chapter, and his expression is: 'If they differ regarding the mahr, judgment is for the one who provides proof; if both provide proof, it is for the woman; if both fail, they take mutual oaths...' except that his statement 'if both provide proof, it is for the woman' is inclusive of the case where the mahr al-mithl is a witness for him, for her, or between them. In the first case [mahr al-mithl supports him], her evidence prevails because it proves an additional amount. As for the second [mahr al-mithl supports her], there is disagreement mentioned in al-Bada'i. It is said: it is as specified in his statement. He said: (I have not seen anyone correct the derivation of al-Razi). He said in al-Nahr: I say: The preference of the commentator and others following the author of al-Hidayah for the derivation of al-Razi indicates its strength, and he corrected it in al-Nihayah. Qadi Khan said: it is preferable. The choice of the author here does not contradict another's choice elsewhere, and interpreting his words here according to what he said in the chapter of mutual oath is apparently far-fetched, because the obligation in this case is that they disagree and mahr al-mithl is adjudged, and there is no indication in his words of this omission. His statement: (because the first of the two obligations) – al-Ramli said: i.e., payment of mahr then submission of her benefit. Some said: judgment is by her evidence also because she showed something that was not apparent by their mutual agreement. As for the appearance by the testimony of mahr al-mithl, it is not considered because we have stated that it is not a proof against others. And some said: judgment is by the husband's evidence; his evidence shows a reduction of a thousand from mahr al-mithl, while her evidence shows nothing because the two thousand was apparent by the testimony of mahr al-mithl. This is the view asserted by al-Zayla'i in the chapter of mutual oath and in this place. As for the third [mahr al-mithl between them], the correct view is that they neutralize each other [tahātarā] because they are equal in claim and proof, then the full mahr al-mithl is mandatory, and the husband has a choice between paying dirhams or dinars, unlike mutual oath because the evidence of each negates the other's specification, so the contract becomes free of specification and mahr al-mithl is mandatory. This is not the case in mutual oath because the amount the husband offers is by agreement and the excess by mahr al-mithl. Thus mentioned by al-Karmati. Qadi Khan mentioned that the amount they agreed upon is mandatory as specified, and the excess as mahr al-mithl, as in mutual oath. The first is apparently correct. In al-Muhit, Muhammad said: A man brings evidence that he married this woman for a thousand, and she brings evidence that he married her for two thousand: the mahr is a thousand. If a man brings evidence that he bought this house for a thousand, and the seller brings evidence that he sold it to him for two thousand, it is for two thousand. The difference is that in sale, both evidences can be acted upon because it is possible he bought it from him first, then bought it from him a second time for two thousand, as will come; this is valid because sale can be rescinded, but marriage cannot be rescinded. Each claims a contract different from what the other claims, so the two evidences neutralize each other, and she gets the thousand by the husband's admission.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where both husband and wife present witnesses (bayyinah) regarding the mahr amount. The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states: if both provide evidence, it is for the woman. The commentator explains that this statement covers three scenarios relative to mahr al-mithl: (1) mahr al-mithl supports the husband's claim, (2) supports the wife's claim, (3) is between them. In scenario (1) where mahr al-mithl agrees with the husband, the wife's evidence still prevails because she proves an additional amount beyond what is evident from mahr al-mithl. In scenario (2) where mahr al-mithl supports the wife, there is disagreement. Some say the wife's evidence prevails because she shows something not apparent by their mutual agreement; the mahr al-mithl is not a proof against others. Others (asserted by al-Zayla'i) say the husband's evidence prevails because his evidence shows a reduction from the mahr al-mithl, while hers shows nothing new since the mahr al-mithl already indicated the higher amount. In scenario (3) where mahr al-mithl falls between both claims, the correct view is that the evidences neutralize each other (tahāturā), and the full mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The husband may choose to pay the amount in dirhams or dinars (currency). This differs from the ruling when parties take mutual oaths (tahaluf). The passage then includes a statement from Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishing marriage from sale: in sale, both evidences can be reconciled by assuming two separate contracts (since sale can be rescinded and re-contracted), but marriage cannot be rescinded, so the evidences cancel out and the husband's admission (of the lower amount) prevails.

Key Terms
التهاتر (al-tahātur): The neutralization of two evidences or claims, resulting in neither being given weight.
بينة (bayyinah): legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary mahr for a woman of similar status, used when the mahr is unspecified or disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage
