B) The wife's evidence prevails because she is the one who receives
C) The evidences neutralize each other and full mahr al-mithl is due
D) They must take mutual oaths

Key Takeaway
When both spouses present evidence in a mahr dispute, the ruling depends on whether mahr al-mithl supports one party or lies between; in the latter case, the evidences neutralize and full mahr al-mithl is due.

Muhammad's Distinction Between Sale and Marriage in Evidence
Reasoning from Imam Muhammad distinguishing evidence handling in sale vs marriage based on rescission possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for conflicting evidence in marriage and sale, explain the underlying legal reasoning based on the possibility of rescission, and apply the same analogy to similar contracts.

Core Idea
Sale can be rescinded and recontracted; marriage cannot—so conflicting evidence in sale can coexist, while in marriage it cannot.

When two parties bring conflicting evidence about the price of a sale or the mahr of a marriage, how does a judge decide? Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani gives a nuanced answer that turns on a fundamental difference between the two contracts: sale can be rescinded, marriage cannot. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and shows how the principle applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Note that in marriage, husband claims mahr of 1,000 and wife claims 2,000. In sale, buyer claims price of 1,000 and seller claims 2,000. Both parties present valid evidence.
The evidence is assumed equally strong, so conflict must be resolved by a legal principle.
2
Note the different outcomes
In marriage, the mahr is set at 1,000 (the husband's admission). In sale, the price is set at 2,000 (the higher claim).
This is opposite of what one might expect: in marriage the lower, in sale the higher.
3
Analyse the reasoning
The key is the possibility of rescission (faskh). In sale, it is possible that two separate contracts occurred: a first sale for 1,000, then rescission and a new sale for 2,000. In marriage, rescission is not possible, so only one contract could have existed.
Thus in sale both pieces of evidence can be valid; in marriage they neutralize each other (tahāturā).
4
Recognise the qiyas (analogy)
The illa (effective cause) is the possibility of rescission. Sale has it, marriage does not. This yields the different rulings. The qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the illa is explicit in the text.
This shows how Hanafi usul uses contract nature to resolve evidence conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط وقال محمد : رجل أقام بينة على أنه تزوج هذه المرأة بألف وأقامت بينة أنه تزوجها على ألفين فالمهر ألف ولو أقام رجل بينة أنه اشترى هذه الدار بألف وأقام البائع بينة أنه باعها منه بألفين فهي بألفين والفرق أن في البيع أمكن العمل بالبيتنين لاحتمال أنه اشترى منه أولاً ثم اشتراها منه بألفين ثانياً كما سيأتي فيصح، لأن البيع يحتمل الفسخ والنكاح لا يحتمل الفسخ وكل منهما ادعى عقداً غير ما ادعاه الآخر فتهاترت البينتان ووجب لها الألف باعتراف الزوج .اهـ.
And in al-Muhit: Muhammad said: A man brings evidence that he married this woman for a thousand, and she brings evidence that he married her for two thousand: the mahr is a thousand. If a man brings evidence that he bought this house for a thousand, and the seller brings evidence that he sold it to him for two thousand, it is for two thousand. The difference is that in sale, both evidences can be acted upon because it is possible he bought it from him first, then bought it from him a second time for two thousand, as will come; this is valid because sale can be rescinded, but marriage cannot be rescinded. Each claims a contract different from what the other claims, so the two evidences neutralize each other, and she gets the thousand by the husband's admission.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage records a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Muhit. He distinguishes between marriage and sale when both parties present conflicting evidence about the price/mahr. In marriage: husband claims mahr of 1,000, wife claims 2,000, both bring witnesses. The result is that the husband's admission (1,000) is taken, because the two evidences neutralize each other (tahāturā). In sale: buyer claims price of 1,000, seller claims 2,000, both bring witnesses. The result is that the sale price is 2,000 (the higher amount). The reason: sale can be rescinded and recontracted. It is possible that two valid contracts occurred: first a sale for 1,000, then a rescission and a new sale for 2,000. Since marriage cannot be rescinded, it is impossible that two different marriage contracts existed with different mahr amounts. Therefore, the husband's admission of 1,000 is binding.

Key Terms
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission or cancellation of a contract.
تهاتر البينتين (tahātur al-bayyinatin): Neutralization of two opposing pieces of evidence such that neither prevails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because marriage requires witnesses for validity, sale does not
B) Because sale can be rescinded and recontracted, but marriage cannot
C) Because the mahr is always the lower amount, while the sale price is always the higher
D) Because in sale, the buyer is always trusted more

Key Takeaway
Conflicting evidence in sale can be reconciled because sale can be rescinded and recontracted; in marriage, evidence cancels and the husband's admission determines the mahr.

Dispute Resolution Based on Type of Mahr
Explains how the ruling on mahr disputes varies depending on whether the mahr is a debt or a specific item.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mahr as a debt versus a specific item and apply the corresponding dispute resolution rule, including the case where quantity is ancillary.

Core Idea
When mahr is a specific item not tied to quantity, the husband's statement is accepted without oaths or mahr al-mithl.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how courts resolve disputes about the quantity of mahr when the marriage contract is silent on evidence. The ruling hinges on whether the mahr is a debt in the dhimmah or a specific physical item, and for specific items, whether the contract treats quantity as integral or ancillary. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion in mahr litigation.

Guided Path
1
Categorise the mahr type
Determine whether the mahr is a debt (dayn) described in the dhimmah or a specific item ('ayn) physically present. This is the primary classification.
Debt is not a tangible object; it is a liability like '10 kilos of wheat'.
2
Apply debt (dayn) rule
If it is a debt, any dispute over quantity is treated like a dispute over currency (dirhams/dinars): both parties take oaths if no evidence exists.
The debt is described by type and amount, so quantity is essential.
3
Sub-classify specific item ('ayn)
If it is a specific item, check whether the contract's validity depends on the quantity. For example, food where the amount is integral (mahr on 'this food, being a kur').
If quantity is integral, the rule is the same as currency disputes.
4
Handle ancillary quantity dispute
If the contract is not tied to quantity (e.g., a specific cloth with a condition on length), no mutual oath is taken, no mahr al-mithl is adjudged, and the husband's statement (lower amount) is accepted by consensus.
The cloth's identity is fixed; the condition is secondary.
5
Identify the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The distinction rests on whether removing part of the item would affect the essence. For a cloth, removing some length does not destroy the cloth; for food, removing quantity changes the subject matter.
This reasoning underlies the consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في القدر فشمل النقد والمكيل والموزون لما في المحيط ولو كان المهر مكيلاً أو موزوناً بعينه فاختلفا في قدر المكيل والموزون والمذروع فهو مثل الاختلاف في الألف والألفين لأنه اختلاف في الذات ألا : إزالة البعض منه لا تنقص الباقي .اهـ. وحاصل الاختلاف في القدر لا يخلو إما أن يكون المهر ديناً أو عيناً، فإن كان ديناً موصوفاً في الذمة بأن تزوجها على مكيل موصوف أو موزون أو مذروع كذلك فاختلفا في قدر المكيل والوزن والذرع فهو كالاختلاف في قدر الدراهم والدنانير، وإن كان عيناً، فإن كان مما يتعلق العقد بقدره، فإن تزوجها على طعام بعينه فاختلفا في قدره فقال الزوج تزوجتك على هذا الطعام على أنه كر فقالت إنه كران فهو كالألف والألفين، وإن كان مما لا يتعلق العقد بقدره بأن تزوجها على ثوب بعينه كل ذراع منه يساوي عشرة دراهم فاختلفا فقال الزوج تزوجتك على هذا الثوب بشرط أنه ثمانية أذرع فقالت بشرط أنه عشرة أذرع لا يتحالفان ولا يحكم مهر المثل والقول قول الزوج بالإجماع. كذا في البدائع .
And he gave an absolute ruling regarding quantity, so it includes cash, measured, and weighed items. According to al-Muhit: if the mahr is a measured or weighed specific item, and they differ on the quantity of the measured, weighed, or cubit-measured item, it is like the difference between one thousand and two thousand, because it is a difference in the essence; removing some of it does not decrease the remainder. The summary of the difference in quantity is that either the mahr is a debt or a specific item. If it is a debt described in the dhimmah, such as he marries her on a described measured, weighed, or cubit-measured item, and they differ on the amount of measure, weight, or cubits, it is like the difference in the amount of dirhams and dinars. If it is a specific item, then if the contract is tied to its quantity, e.g., he marries her on a specific food, then they differ on its amount: the husband says 'I married you on this food, it being a kur' and she says 'it is two kur,' it is like the case of one thousand and two thousand. If the contract is not tied to its quantity, e.g., he marries her on a specific cloth, each cubit of which is worth ten dirhams, and they differ: the husband says 'I married you on this cloth on condition it is eight cubits' and she says 'on condition it is ten cubits,' then they do not take mutual oaths, nor is mahr al-mithl adjudged, and the husband's statement is taken by consensus. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage categorizes mahr disputes based on whether the mahr is a debt (dīn) in the dhimmah or a specific item ('ayn). If it is a debt (e.g., described as '10 kilos of wheat'), the dispute over quantity is treated like a dispute over currency (dirhams/dinars): both parties take oaths if no evidence. If it is a specific item, further subdivision: (a) if the contract's validity depends on the quantity (like food where quantity is integral), the dispute is again like the currency case; (b) if the contract is not tied to the quantity (e.g., a specific cloth where the condition of length is ancillary), then no mutual oath is needed, mahr al-mithl is not applied, and the husband's statement (the lower amount) is accepted by consensus. The reasoning: in the latter case, the item is defined by its identity, not its quantity; the condition about length is secondary, so the husband's word is taken. This ruling is from al-Bada'i.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A debt or obligation in the dhimmah, described by type and quantity.
عين ('ayn): A specific physical object, like a particular cloth or food item.
مكيل (makil): A measured item by volume (e.g., grains).
موزون (mawzun): A weighed item (e.g., gold, wheat by weight).
مذروع (madhrū'): An item measured by cubit (length), e.g., cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They must take mutual oaths and then mahr al-mithl is applied
B) The wife's statement is taken because she is the recipient
C) No mutual oath, no mahr al-mithl, and the husband's statement is accepted by consensus
D) The cloth is divided proportionally

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for mahr quantity disputes depends on whether the mahr is a debt or a specific item, and for specific items, whether quantity is integral or ancillary—in the ancillary case, the husband's word is accepted by consensus.

Ruling When Both Spouses Present Conflicting Evidence on Mahr
Explaining the ruling when both spouses have conflicting evidence on mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when both spouses present conflicting evidence on the mahr, explain the reasoning of tahatur (cancellation), and distinguish this case from a sale transaction.

Core Idea
When both spouses have conflicting evidence on the mahr, the evidences cancel, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario in marriage contracts where the husband and wife disagree on the mahr amount and each brings witnesses. The commentator explores various Hanafi opinions and establishes the preferred position that the evidences cancel out, leading to the obligation of mahr al-mithl. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the concept of tahatur and the distinction between marriage and sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial opinions
Read the passage noting that some scholars favor the wife's evidence, others the husband's. Al-Zayla'i is cited as supporting the husband's evidence.
2
Understand the third position: cancellation (tahatur)
The correct view is that when both have evidence, they cancel each other because they are equal in claim and proof. The contract is then considered without a specified mahr.
Tahatur means mutual cancellation.
3
Determine the consequence: mahr al-mithl
Since no specific mahr remains, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (equitable dower). The husband may choose to pay in dirhams or dinars.
This is unlike mutual oath (tahaluf) where the husband would pay the amount he claims.
4
Compare with sale transaction
In a sale, if both parties have conflicting evidence, both can be upheld because sale permits rescission and multiple contracts. Marriage does not permit rescission, so cancellation is necessary.
This distinction is made by Imam Muhammad in al-Muhit.
5
Note the scope: when evidence is about the mahr only, not the contract
The discussion applies when evidence is about the mahr amount, not when testimony includes the contract itself with a specified mahr.
If testimony includes the contract, the ruling differs.

Because the Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr: Some of them said: Judgment is given by her evidence also because she showed something that wasn't apparent by their agreement. As for appearance through testimony of mahr al-mithl, it is not considered because we have stated that it is not a proof against others. And some said: Judgment is given by the husband's evidence; his evidence shows a reduction of one thousand from mahr al-mithl, and her evidence shows nothing because the two thousand were apparent through testimony of mahr al-mithl. This opinion is firmly held by al-Zayla'i in the chapter of mutual oath and in this place. As for the third case, when evidence is between them (i.e., both have evidence), the correct position is that they cancel each other out because they are equal in claim and proof, then the entire mahr al-mithl is due, and the husband may choose between paying dirhams or dinars, unlike the case of mutual oath (tahaluf). This is because each party's evidence negates the other's specification, so the contract is void of specification, thus mahr al-mithl is due. It is not like mutual oath because the obligation of the amount the husband offers is by agreement, and the excess is by mahr al-mithl; thus mentioned by al-Karmati. Qadi Khan mentioned that the amount agreed upon is due as specified mahr, and the excess as mahr al-mithl, like in mutual oath, but the first view is evident. In al-Muhit: Muhammad said: A man presented evidence that he married this woman for one thousand, and she presented evidence that he married her for two thousand; the mahr is one thousand. If a man presented evidence that he bought this house for one thousand, and the seller presented evidence that he sold it to him for two thousand, it is for two thousand. The difference is that in sale, it is possible to act on both evidences due to the possibility that he bought from him first and then bought it from him again for two thousand, as will come, so it is valid, because sale permits rescission, but marriage does not permit rescission. Each claimed a contract different from what the other claimed, so the two evidences cancel each other, and she gets one thousand by the husband's admission. End. If this statement of Muhammad is a transmission of the school, not his sole opinion, then the meaning of their statement 'If they present evidence, then for the woman' applies when his evidence testifies that the mahr is one thousand and her evidence testifies that the mahr is two thousand, and the testimony does not include the contract. As for when the testimony includes the contract with a specified mahr, its ruling is known. From this, you see that his statement: (We restricted by the condition that no evidence is established) i.e., by his statement in the beginning of the discourse: 'And neither has evidence'. His statement: (So the meaning of their statement, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And it is not hidden what is in it, so ponder it. His statement: (So its ruling is known) i.e., from what al-Muhit transmitted from Muhammad.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the scenario where both spouses present conflicting evidence regarding the amount of mahr in a marriage contract. The commentator expands on the ruling by first noting differing opinions among Hanafi scholars. Some hold that the wife's evidence should prevail because it reveals something not previously apparent (the higher amount), while others side with the husband's evidence. Al-Zayla'i is cited as firmly adopting the latter view. However, the correct position (sahih) in the third case—when both have evidence—is that the two pieces of evidence cancel each other (tahatur), because they are equal in claim and proof. Consequently, the contract is considered devoid of a specified mahr, and the husband must pay the full mahr al-mithl (equitable dower). The husband is given a choice between paying in dirhams or dinars, unlike in mutual oath (tahaluf) where the husband would pay what he claims. The passage then cites a ruling from Imam Muhammad via al-Muhit, distinguishing the case of marriage from sale. In sale, both evidences can be reconciled because the transaction may have been repeated; in marriage, rescission is not possible, so the evidences cancel. The marginal note clarifies that the author Kanz al-Daqaiq restricted the discussion to cases where no evidence is established, and this commentary is explaining the ruling when evidence is present.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence (usually two male witnesses) presented in court to prove a claim.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dower determined by considering the mahr of women similar to the wife (e.g., paternal female relatives).
تهاتر (tahatur): The cancellation of mutual claims or evidences due to equivalence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When both spouses present conflicting evidence on the mahr amount in a marriage contract, what is the Hanafi ruling according to the preferred view in this passage?
A) The wife's evidence prevails, so she gets the higher amount.
B) The husband's evidence prevails, so he pays the lower amount.
C) The evidences cancel each other, and the husband pays mahr al-mithl.
D) The evidences are combined, and the average amount is paid.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting evidence on mahr is presented by both spouses, the evidences cancel, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl, not the claimed amounts.

Debt vs Specific Item Mahr Disputes
Classifying mahr disputes and their legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish whether a disputed mahr is a debt or a specific item and apply the Hanafi ruling for disputes over genus, type, or description.

Core Idea
Debt mahr disputes over genus/type/description void the specification; specific item disputes are like amount disputes.

When spouses dispute what was specified as mahr, the first question is whether the mahr was a debt (dayn) or a specific item ('ayn). This classification determines the entire legal analysis. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling for each category, including the special treatment of dirhams and dinars.

Guided Path
1
Classify the mahr as debt or specific item
Determine whether the specified mahr is an obligation in the husband's liability (dayn) or a tangible object ('ayn). The ruling flows from this classification.
Examples of debt: '1000 dirhams', 'a kur of wheat'. Examples of specific item: 'this slave', 'this garment'.
2
If debt, identify the subject of dispute
Is the dispute over genus (jins), type (naw'), or description (sifah)? Each leads to the same result: the specification is invalid, and mahr al-mithl is due.
Exception: dirhams vs dinars are treated as dispute over amount, not genus.
3
If specific item, apply the amount-dispute rule
Dispute over genus/type/description of a specific item is analogous to dispute over amount (e.g., 1000 vs 2000). The husband's word is accepted unless the wife's mahr al-mithl is higher.
If the wife's mahr al-mithl is higher, she gets the value of what she claimed, not the item itself.
4
Note the exception for dirhams and dinars
Even though dirhams and dinars are different genera, they are treated as one genus in mahr al-mithl calculations. Thus, a dispute over '1000 dirhams vs 100 dinars' is treated as an amount dispute.
This rule applies only in the chapter of mahr, not in sales.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه واردة على إطلاق المصنف، وجوابه أن القدر في الثوب وإن كان من أجزائه حقيقة لكنه جارٍ مجرى الوصف وهو صفة الجودة شرعاً لأنه يوجب صفة الجودة لغيره ره من الأجزاء، ولذا كان الزائد للمشتري فيما إذا باعه وعين قدراً فوجده أزيد والأصل أن ما يوجب فوات بعضه نقصاناً في البقية فهو كالوصف، كما علم في البيوع، وصرح به في البدائع هنا . وقيد بالقدر لأنه لو اختلفا في جنس المهر أو نوعه أو صفته فإنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون المسمى ديناً أو عيناً، فإن كان ديناً فإن كان في الجنس كما إذا قال تزوجتك على عبد فقالت على جارية، أو قال على كر شعير فقالت على كر حنطة أو على ثياب هروية، أو قال على ألف درهم وقالت على مائة دينار على هذا العبد وقالت المرأة على هذه الجارية فهو كالاختلاف في الألف والألفين إلا في فصل واحد وهو ما إذا كان مهر مثلها مثل قيمة الجارية أو أكثر فلها قيمة الجارية لا عينها لأن تمليك الجارية لا يكون إلا بالتراضي ولم يتفقا على تمليكها فلم يوجد الرضا من صاحب الجارية بتمليكها فتعذر التسليم فيقضي بقيمتها بخلاف ما إذا اختلفا في الدراهم والدنانير فإنه نظير الاختلاف في الألف والألفين على معنى أن مهر مثلها اهـ. يعني يجب مهر المثل ولا يخفى ما فيه من المخالفة لما في البدائع وفي الظهيرية : ولو اختلفا في الوصف والقدر جميعاً فالقول للزوج في الوصف والقول للمرأة في القدر إلى تمام مهر مثلها . وفي المحيط وغيره، لو تصادقا على مهر عين كالعبد ثم هلك عند الزوج فاختلفا في القيمة فالقول قول من عليه الدين وهو الزوج. وفي الخانية : لو قالت المرأة تزوجتني على عبدك هذا وقال الرجل تزوجتك على أمتي هذه وهي أم المرأة وأقاما البينة فالبينة بينة المرأة لأن بينتها قامت على حق نفسها وبيئة الزوج قامت على حق الغير وتعتق الأمة على الزوج بإقراره اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : رجل وامرأة في أيديهما دار فأقامت المرأة البينة أن الدار والجواب أنه يجوز كونه مكاتباً أو مأذوناً مديوناً أو نحو ذلك .
And this applies to the author's general statement. The answer is that quantity in a garment, although actually part of its parts, is treated as a description, and it is a quality of goodness legally, because it causes a quality of goodness for its other parts. Hence, the excess belongs to the buyer when he sells it having specified a quantity and finds it more. The principle is that what causes the loss of some parts to be a deficiency in the rest is like a description, as known in sales, and stated in al-Bada'i' here. It is restricted to quantity because if they dispute over the genus, type, or description of the mahr, then it is either that the specified is a debt or a specific item. If it is a debt, then if it is over genus – such as if he said 'I married you for a slave' and she said 'for a slave-girl', or he said 'for a kur of barley' and she said 'for a kur of wheat' or 'for Herawi garments', or he said 'for one thousand dirhams' and she said 'for one hundred dinars' – or if over type – like Turkish and Roman, Egyptian dinars and Suwari dinars – or over description – like quality and poor quality – then the dispute over it is like dispute over two different items, except dirhams and dinars; dispute over them is like dispute over one thousand and two thousand. This is because each of the two genera, types, or described items cannot be owned except by mutual consent, unlike dirhams and dinars; although they are two different genera, they are treated as one genus in the chapter of mahr al-mithl. If the specified is a specific item – such as he said 'I married you for this slave' and she said 'for this slave-girl' – it is like dispute over one thousand and two thousand, except for one distinction: if her mahr al-mithl is equal to the value of the slave-girl or more, she gets the value of the slave-girl, not the slave-girl itself, because ownership of the slave-girl is only by mutual consent and they did not agree on its ownership, so consent from the owner of the slave-girl is absent, delivery is impossible, so its value is decreed. Unlike if they dispute over dirhams and dinars, it is analogous to dispute over one thousand and two thousand in the sense that if her mahr al-mithl is equal to one hundred dinars or more, she gets one hundred dinars. Thus in al-Bada'i' also. In al-Muhit it is mentioned: Dispute over genus, type, or description: if the specified is a specific item, the husband's word is accepted; if it is a debt, it is like dispute over the original (i.e., mahr al-mithl is due). End. That is, mahr al-mithl is due, and it is not hidden that there is contradiction with what is in al-Bada'i'. In al-Zahiriyyah: If they dispute over description and quantity together, the husband's word is accepted regarding description, and the woman's word regarding quantity up to the full amount of her mahr al-mithl. In al-Muhit and others: If they agree on a specific mahr like a slave, then it perishes with the husband, and they dispute over its value, the word of the one who owes the debt (i.e., the husband) is accepted. In al-Khaniyyah: If a woman says 'You married me on this slave of yours' and the man says 'I married you on this slave-girl of mine – who is the mother of the woman – and they present evidence, then the woman's evidence prevails because her evidence is about her own right, and the husband's evidence is about the right of another (the slave-girl). The slave-girl becomes free by the husband's admission. End. In al-Zahiriyyah: A man and woman have a house in their hands. The woman presents evidence that the house is hers and the man is her slave. The man presents evidence that the house is his and the woman is his wife, but he does not present evidence that he is free. Then the woman's evidence prevails, and the house and slave are hers. And his statement: (And he did not present evidence that he is free.) Al-Maqdisi said: Therein that the house being his implies his freedom. The answer is that it is possible he is a mukatib, or a ma'dhun in debt, or similar.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage addresses disputes between spouses over the mahr when it is specified as a particular item or debt. The commentator explains that quantity in a specific item (e.g., a garment) is treated as a description, not as a separate entity. Therefore, if a seller sells a garment specifying a length, and the buyer finds it longer, the excess belongs to the seller. Similarly, in mahr disputes, quantity is akin to a description of quality. The key distinction is whether the mahr is a debt (dayn) or a specific item ('ayn). If it is a debt (e.g., owed in the abstract), then disputes over genus (e.g., slave vs. slave-girl), type (e.g., Turkish vs. Roman), or description (e.g., high vs. low quality) are treated as disputes over entirely different items, meaning the contract is invalid as to specification, and mahr al-mithl becomes due. An exception is dirhams and dinars, which are treated as one genus for mahr al-mithl purposes. If the mahr is a specific item (e.g., 'this slave'), then dispute over genus/type/description is like dispute over amount (e.g., one thousand vs. two thousand), with the husband's word accepted unless the wife's mahr al-mithl is higher. Additional rulings from al-Bada'i', al-Muhit, al-Zahiriyyah, and al-Khaniyyah are cited: when both description and quantity are disputed, the husband's word on description and wife's word on quantity (up to mahr al-mithl); when a specified item perishes and value is disputed, the husband's word is accepted; conflicting evidence on ownership of a slave-girl favors the wife; and a case where a man and woman dispute ownership of a house and status of the man as slave or free, with the woman's evidence prevailing.

Key Terms
المسمى ديناً (al-musamma daynan): The appointed mahr as a debt, i.e., a liability in the husband's obligation, not a specific item.
المسمى عيناً (al-musamma 'aynan): The appointed mahr as a specific tangible item (e.g., a particular slave).
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dower determined by comparison to female relatives; used when mahr is unspecified or disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband and wife dispute over the type of a debt mahr (e.g., Turkish vs. Roman slave), what is the outcome according to al-Bada'i'?
A) The husband's word is accepted.
B) The wife gets the item she claimed.
C) Mahr al-mithl becomes due.
D) The marriage is void.

Key Takeaway
The classification of mahr as debt or specific item determines the ruling for disputes over genus, type, description, and quantity, with dirhams and dinars treated as one genus.

Resolving Mahr Disputes Before Consummation: Mut'ah, Tahkim, and the Hanafi Intra-School Difference
Explaining the Hanafi intra-school dispute on mut'ah when mahr amount is disputed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr disputes before consummation and distinguish between the views of Abu Yusuf, the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, and the relied-upon position, including the distinction between dayn and 'ayn.

Core Idea
When mahr is disputed, the wife takes half of what the husband admits; mut'ah arbitration only applies when no specification exists or when the mahr is a specific item.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement about how to resolve a dispute over the mahr amount when a divorce occurs before consummation. The core issue is whether the husband's word alone (with oath) suffices, or whether arbitration of mut'ah (tahkim) is needed. The commentary reconciles conflicting narrations and establishes the preferred ruling that balances certainty and fairness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the procedural context
Recognize that the dispute arises after a divorce before consummation. The wife is entitled to half the mahr (if specified) or mut'ah (if not). The question is: when both spouses claim different amounts, how is the half determined?
The rule of 'half the mahr' is fixed; the dispute is over the base amount.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
According to the narration in al-Jami' al-Kabir, Abu Yusuf holds that the husband's word (with oath) is taken, unless he claims an extremely low (munkar) amount. This means the wife gets half of what the husband admits, and the husband swears to deny the excess.
This is based on the principle that the party being asked (the husband) is believed.
3
State the second narration
The narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir states the husband's word is taken regarding half the mahr without any arbitration of mut'ah. This implies the wife gets half of what the husband says, but no additional tahkim for mut'ah.
This version omits the possibility of tahkim entirely.
4
Explain the reconciliation attempt
The author of al-Hidayah attempts to reconcile these by noting that the original case (al-Asl) involved large amounts (thousands) where mut'ah is negligible, while al-Jami' al-Kabir dealt with small amounts where mut'ah matters. Thus the conflicting rulings are context-dependent.
The reconciliation is criticized by later scholars as not fully resolving the difference.
5
Identify the relied-upon position and its rationale
The majority of later Hanafi authorities (al-Bada'i', Sharh al-Tahawi, Fath al-Qadir) prefer the view that the wife takes half of what the husband acknowledges, and he swears for the excess. Crucially, they distinguish based on the nature of the mahr: if it is a debt (dayn), half is certain; if it is a specific item ('ayn), ownership is uncertain, so mut'ah by tahkim applies unless the husband agrees to give half the item.
This position respects the agreement on specification (tasmiya) while also handling uncertainty.

قوله : (والمتعة لو طلقها قبل الوطء أي حكمت المتعة فإن شهدت لأحدهما فالقول قوله مع يمينه، وإن كانت بين نصف ما يدعيه ونصف ما تدعيه المرأة حلف كل واحد منهما كما في حال قيام النكاح. وعند أبي يوسف القول قول الزوج مع يمينه إلا أن يأتي بشيء مستنكر كما قدمناه وهذا على رواية الجامع الكبير وهو قياس قولهما. وفي رواية الجامع الصغير : والأصل القول قول الزوج في نصف المهر من غير تحكيم للمتعة. وفي الهداية : ووجه التوفيق أنه وضع المسألة في الأصل في الألف والألفين والمتعة لا تبلغ هذا المبلغ في العادة فلا يفيد تحكيمها. ووضعها في الجامع الكبير في العشرة والمائة ومتعة مثلها عشرون فيفيد التحكيم، والمذكور في الجامع الصغير ساكت عن ذكر المقدار فيحمل على ما هو المذكور في الأصل .اهـ. وصحح في البدائع وشرح الطحاوي أنه يتنصف ما قال الزوج، ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن المتعة موجبة فيما إذا لم يكن فيه تسمية وهنا اتفقا على التسمية فقلنا ببقاء ما اتفقا عليه وهو نصف ما أقربه الزوج ويحلف على نفي دعواها الزائد، وأراد بتحكيم المتعة فيما إذا كان المسمى ديناً، أما إذا كان عيناً كما في مسألة العبد والجارية فلها المتعة تحكيم إلا أن يرضى الزوج أن تأخذ نصف الجارية بخلاف ما إذا اختلفا في الألف والألفين لأن نصف الألف ثابت بيقين لاتفاقهما على تسمية الألف والملك في نصف الجارية ليس بثابت بيقين لأنهما لم يتفقا على تسمية أحدهما فلا يمكن القضاء بنصف الجارية إلا باختيارهما، فإذا لم يوجد سقط البدلان فوجب الرجوع إلى المتعة. كذا في البدائع . من غير وجوب تحكيم المتعة يرجع إلى قوله : (وفي الهداية ووجه التوفيق الخ قال في الفتح : وحاصله. إلا في موضع يكون ما اعترف به أكثر منها فيؤخذ باعترافه ويعطى نصف مهر المثل قوله: (ويحلف على نفس دعواها (الزائد قال في الفتح بعده: وعلى هذا فلا ذلك التوفيق بل يتحقق الخلاف ولهذا قيل في المسألة روايتان، لكن ما ذكر في جواب قول أبي يوسف آنفاً يدفعه ا هـ . والذي ذكره يتم
His saying: (And the mut'ah if he divorces her before consummation) i.e., the mut'ah is determined by arbitration. If one of them testifies, then the word is his with his oath. If it is between half of what he claims and half of what she claims, each of them swears, as in the case of the existence of the marriage. According to Abu Yusuf, the word is that of the husband with his oath, unless he brings something objectionable, as we have presented, and this is according to the narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir, and it is the qiyas of their saying. In the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir: The principle is that the husband's word is taken regarding half the mahr without arbitration of mut'ah. In al-Hidayah: The way of reconciliation is that he placed the issue in al-Asl in thousands and two thousands, and mut'ah does not reach this amount normally, so arbitration is not beneficial. He placed it in al-Jami' al-Kabir in ten and one hundred, and the mut'ah of its like is twenty, so arbitration is beneficial. What is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir is silent about mentioning the amount, so it is interpreted according to what is mentioned in al-Asl. End quote. And it was corrected in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Tahawi that it is half of what the husband said, and it was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because mut'ah is obligatory when there is no specification, and here they agreed on the specification, so we say that what they agreed upon remains, which is half of what the husband acknowledged, and he swears to deny her additional claim. He intended by arbitration of mut'ah when the specified is a debt, but if it is a specific item as in the issue of the male slave and female slave, then she has mut'ah by arbitration unless the husband agrees that she takes half the female slave, unlike when they disputed in the thousands and two thousands because half of the thousand is established with certainty due to their agreement on specifying the thousand, while ownership in half the female slave is not established with certainty because they did not agree on specifying either of them, so it is not possible to decree half the female slave except by their choice. If it is not found, the alternatives fall and it is necessary to return to mut'ah. Thus in al-Bada'i'. Without the obligation of arbitration of mut'ah, it returns to his saying: (In al-Hidayah and the way of reconciliation...). He said in al-Fath: Its summary is: except in a place where what he acknowledges is more than it, then his acknowledgment is taken and half the proper dower is given. His saying: (And he swears regarding the denial of her additional claim). He said in al-Fath after it: And upon this, that reconciliation does not hold, but rather the disagreement is realized, and for this it was said that there are two narrations in the issue, but what was mentioned in response to the saying of Abu Yusuf earlier refutes it. End quote. And what he mentioned is complete.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement regarding the rule of mut'ah (a gift given to a wife divorced before consummation) when the parties dispute the amount of the mahr (dower). The author explains that if the dispute is over the existence of the specified mahr, the word of the one who denies the claim is accepted with oath. If they dispute over half of what each claims, both must swear. Then the text presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement. According to Abu Yusuf on the narration of al-Jami' al-Kabir, the husband's word with oath is taken unless the amount he claims is extremely low (munkar). In the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, the husband's word is taken regarding half the mahr without any arbitration of mut'ah. Al-Hidayah attempts to reconcile these two narrations by noting that in al-Asl (by Imam Muhammad) the amounts in question are large (thousands), so the mut'ah (which is typically small) does not justify arbitration. In al-Jami' al-Kabir, the amounts are small (ten or one hundred), so mut'ah is significant and arbitration is useful. Al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Tahawi prefer the ruling that the wife receives half of what the husband acknowledges, and he swears for any excess. Fath al-Qadir supports this because mut'ah is only applicable when there is no specification (tasmiya) of the mahr; here they agreed on a specification (the husband's acknowledged amount), so the agreed half is taken. Then the commentary distinguishes between a mahr that is a debt (dayn) and a specific item ('ayn). If the mahr is a specific item (e.g., a slave), the wife cannot be forced to take half of it because ownership is not certain; thus the only option is to return to mut'ah unless the husband agrees to give half. The passage concludes with a further discussion of the reconciliation and critique from al-Fath, indicating that the reconciliation is not fully accepted and that there are indeed two narrations, but the earlier response to Abu Yusuf's view refutes the need for reconciliation.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A gift given by the husband to the wife upon divorce before consummation, as compensation, equivalent to what is appropriate for her status.
تحكيم (tahkim): Arbitration; referring to determining the amount of mut'ah by considering the status of the woman and her family, not by the specified mahr.
مستنكر (mustankar): Something extremely low or unusual; if the husband claims an amount that is absurdly low, his word is not accepted even with oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the husband admits to a mahr of 500 dirhams (debt) and the wife claims 1000 dirhams, what does the wife receive after divorce before consummation?
A) 500 dirhams (the full admitted amount)
B) 250 dirhams (half of the admitted amount)
C) A mut'ah determined by tahkim
D) 0 dirhams, unless the husband agrees

Key Takeaway
When a mahr dispute arises before consummation, the Hanafi school's preferred ruling gives the wife half of what the husband admits, shifting to mut'ah arbitration only when the mahr is a specific item.

Mahr al-Mithl When the Named Mahr Is Disputed
Sharh on Kanz al-Daqaiq explaining mahr al-mithl when the named mahr is disputed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when spouses dispute the existence of a named mahr and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the requirement of an oath.

Core Idea
When the named mahr is disputed, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib by consensus, but the need for an oath before giving it divides Abu Hanifa from his disciples.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: if a husband and wife disagree over whether a specific mahr was agreed upon, the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. While all Hanafi imams agree on this point, a significant intra-madhhab dispute arises over whether the denying spouse must take an oath before mahr al-mithl is determined. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the reasoning and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute type
Distinguish between a dispute over the existence of a named mahr (as here) and a dispute over the amount of an acknowledged mahr. In this case, one spouse claims a specific mahr was agreed, the other denies any agreement.
This affects the application of rules about oaths and the determination of mahr al-mithl.
2
State the consensus on mahr al-mithl
The passage states that mahr al-mithl is wajib 'by agreement' (ittifaqan) when the named mahr is disputed. This consensus is the primary proof.
Consensus (ijma) within the Hanafi school is a binding proof.
3
Unpack the intra-Hanafi oath dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is required in marriage matters, so mahr al-mithl is given directly. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require the denier to swear; if he refuses, the named amount stands; if he swears, mahr al-mithl is given.
The oath is seen as pertaining to property (mahr), not the marriage contract itself.
4
Analyse the tarjih (preferred view)
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) prefer the requirement of an oath, aligning with general rules for property disputes. This is the mufta bihi position.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa's view, mahr al-mithl is immediate; under the other view, the wife may establish the named amount if the husband refuses to swear.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a case: wife claims a named mahr of 1000 dirhams, husband denies. The judge asks the husband to swear. If he swears, mahr al-mithl is determined; if he refuses, he pays 1000 dirhams.
The mahr al-mithl is bounded by the claims: not more than the wife's claim if she is the claimant, not less than the husband's claim if he is the claimant.

قوله : (ولو) في أصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل أي ولو اختلفا في أصل المسمى بأن ادعاه أحدهما ونفاه الآخر فإنه يجب مهر المثل اتفاقاً والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الدخول اتفاقاً، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن أحدهما يدعي التسمية والآخر ينكره فالقول قول المنكر، وكذا عند أبي يوسف لتعذر القضاء بالمسمى بخلاف ما تقدم لأنه أمكن القضاء بالمتفق وهو الأقل ما لم يكن مستنكراً. وقوله في الهداية «لأن مهر المثل هو الأصل عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد مشكل لأنه قدم قبله أن المسمى هو الأصل عند محمد وإنما مهر المثل هو الأصل عند الإمام فقط . كذا ذكره الشارحون . وجوابه أنه الأصل في التحكيم عندهما كما . في الاختلاف في القدر وليس مراده الاصالة بالنسبة إلى المسمى فلا إشكال أطلقه فشمل الاختلاف في حياتهما وبعد موت أحدهما سواء كان في الأصل أو في القدر، فحكم الاختلاف بعد موت أحدهما في القدر كهو في حياتهما كما في المحيط ، وأما في الأصل فقال في التبيين ولو كان الاختلاف بعد موت أحدهما فالجواب فيه كالجواب في حياتهما بالاتفاق لأن اعتبار مهر المثل لا يسقط بموت أحدهما وكذا لو طلقها قبل الدخول اهـ. يعني تحكم المتعة. وفي البزازية ادعت المسمى بعد موته فأقر الوارث به لكن قال لا أعرف قدره حبس، وظاهر كلام المصنف أنه يجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وليس كذلك، بل لا يزاد على ما ادعته المرأة لو كانت هي المدعية للتسمية ولا ينقص عما ادعاه الزوج لو كان هو المدعى لها كما أشار إليه في البدائع، ولم يتعرض الشارحون للتحليف. وذكر صدر الشريعة أنه يحلف عندهما، فإن نكل ثبت المسمى، وإن حلف المنكر وجب مهر المثل، وأما عند أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يحلف المنكر لأنه لا تحليف عنده في النكاح فيجب مهر المثل اهـ. وفيه نظر لأن التحليف هنا على المال لا على أصل النكاح فيتعين أن يحلف منكر التسمية إجماعاً ولهذا سكتوا قبيله نصه : وأما قوله تيقناً التسمية وهي ما أقربه الزوج فليس بذاك بل المتيقن أحدهما غير عين وهو لا ينفي الرجوع إذ لا فرق بين ذلك وعدم التسمية حيث تعذر القضاء بأحدهما عيناً ا هـ. وقوله وهو لا ينفي الرجوع أي كون المتيقن غير عين لا ينفي الرجوع إلى الأصل وهو هنا المتعة، وبه يظهر ما في قول المؤلف ورجحه في فتح القدير . قوله (وجوابه أنه الأصل في التحكيم) ينبو عن هذا الجواب قول الهداية إنه الموجب الأصلي في باب النكاح وعن هذا قال في النهر : وقد مر فيما لو تزوجها على هذا العبد أو على هذا العبد ما يغنيك عن هذا الجواب وما فيه من التعسف قوله (حبس) أي حتى يبين لقيامه مقام الزوج. كذا في البزازية قوله (وفيه نظر سبقه إليه صاحب الدرر وتبعه ابن الكمال قال نوح أفندي : وأجاب عنه بعض الفضلاء في حواشي صدر الشريعة فقال : لا يقال إن الكلام في النكاح دون المهر ويجري الحلف في المال اتفاقاً كما المصنف سیصرح به في كتاب الدعوى بقوله إن ادعت المرأة» إلى قوله يلزم المال» لأنا نقول ما ذكره هناك رواية وما ذكره الشارح ههنا دراية وقد رمز إليه بقوله : ينبغي وجه الدراية ههنا عدم نفع التحليف عند النكول إذ الأصل فيه عنده مهر المثل دون المسمى فيجب
His saying: (And if) regarding the original named mahr, the proper dower is obligatory. That is, if they dispute over the original named mahr, one claiming it and the other denying it, then the proper dower is obligatory by agreement, and the mut'ah if he divorces her before consummation is also by agreement. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent because one claims the specification and the other denies it, so the word is that of the denier. Similarly, according to Abu Yusuf, because it is impossible to decree the named amount, unlike what preceded because it was possible to decree the agreed upon amount, which is the lesser, unless it is objectionable. His saying in al-Hidayah, 'because the proper dower is the original according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad' is problematic because he previously stated that the named amount is the original according to Muhammad, and the proper dower is the original only according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). Thus stated the commentators. Its answer is that it is the original in arbitration according to them, as in the dispute over the amount, and he does not mean originality relative to the named amount, so there is no problem. He released it to include the dispute during their lifetimes and after the death of one of them, whether regarding the original or the amount. So the ruling of the dispute after the death of one of them regarding the amount is the same as during their lifetimes, as in al-Muhit. As for the original, it is stated in al-Tabyin: if the dispute occurs after the death of one of them, the answer is the same as during their lifetimes by agreement, because the consideration of the proper dower does not drop due to the death of one of them. Similarly, if he divorced her before consummation, i.e., the mut'ah is governed by arbitration. In al-Bazzaziyya: She claimed the named amount after his death, and the heir acknowledged it but said he did not know its amount; he is imprisoned. The apparent meaning of the author's statement is that the proper dower is obligatory whatever it may be, but it is not so. Rather, it is not increased beyond what the woman claimed if she is the one claiming the specification, nor decreased below what the husband claimed if he is the one who claimed for her, as indicated in al-Bada'i'. The commentators did not address the oath. Sadr al-Shari'ah mentioned that he swears according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and if he refuses, the named amount is established, and if the denier swears, the proper dower is obligatory. According to Abu Hanifa, it is appropriate that the denier should not swear because, according to him, there is no oath in marriage, so the proper dower is obligatory. It is subject to consideration because the oath here pertains to property, not to the marriage itself, so it is determined that the denier of the specification must swear by consensus, and for this reason they remained silent. Shortly before it, his text: 'As for his saying, the certain thing is the specification, which is what the husband acknowledges, that is not correct; rather, the certain thing is one of them, not a specific item, and that does not negate the return, for there is no difference between that and the absence of specification when it becomes impossible to decree either as a specific item.' End quote. And his saying, 'and it does not negate the return' means that the fact that the certain thing is not a specific item does not negate the return to the original, which here is the mut'ah. By this, what is in the author's statement and his preferring in Fath al-Qadir becomes clear. His saying (and its answer is that it is the original in arbitration) - the statement of al-Hidayah, 'it is the original cause in the chapter of marriage,' recoils from this answer. Concerning this, it is said in al-Nahr: There has already passed regarding the case of marrying on this male slave or this female slave what suffices you from this answer and its difficulty. His saying (imprisoned) means until he clarifies, because he stands in the place of the husband. Thus in al-Bazzaziyya. His saying (and it is subject to consideration) - Sadr al-Shari'ah preceded him in it, and Ibn al-Kamal followed him. Nuh Afandi said: Some virtuous scholars answered it in the glosses of Sadr al-Shari'ah, saying: It should not be said that the discussion is about marriage, not the mahr, and the oath applies in property matters by agreement, as the author will explicitly state in the Book of Claims with his saying, 'if the woman claims ... until the property becomes binding.' For we say what he mentioned there is a narration, and what the commentator mentioned here is a rational understanding, and he alluded to it with his saying: 'The aspect of rational understanding here is that the oath, if refused, is of no benefit because the original according to him is the proper dower, not the named amount, so it becomes obligatory.'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement that if the spouses dispute the very existence of a named mahr (i.e., one claims a specific mahr was agreed upon and the other denies it), then the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory. The author explains that this ruling is by agreement (ittifaq) among the Hanafi imams. The reason is that the one who denies the specification has his word accepted, so the named amount cannot be established. This is analogous to Abu Yusuf's view in the previous discussion, except that here it is not possible to decree even the lesser amount because the denial is of any specification, not just the amount. The text then notes a difficulty in al-Hidayah's statement that 'mahr al-mithl is the original according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad' because earlier it was stated that the named mahr is the original according to Muhammad. The answer given is that 'original' here means original in arbitration (tahkim) when the amount is disputed, not that mahr al-mithl is the primary obligation over a specified mahr. The ruling applies whether the dispute occurs during the spouses' lifetimes or after the death of one, and whether it is about the existence or the amount. After death, the same rules apply. The text then discusses a case from al-Bazzaziyya where the wife claims a named mahr after the husband's death, and the heir acknowledges it but does not know the amount; the heir is imprisoned until he clarifies. The author cautions that the seeming implication of the matn (that mahr al-mithl is given without limit) is not correct; rather, the amount is bounded by the wife's claim if she is the claimant, and by the husband's claim if he is the claimant, as mentioned in al-Bada'i'. The commentary then addresses the issue of oaths (tahlif). According to Sadr al-Shari'ah, if the dispute is in the presence of the spouses (or their heirs), the denier must swear according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. If he refuses, the named amount is established; if he swears, mahr al-mithl is given. According to Abu Hanifa, the denier should not be required to swear because he does not administer oaths in marriage matters; thus mahr al-mithl is given directly. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq points out a consideration (nazar) because the oath here is about property (the mahr), not about the marriage itself, so the denier should swear by consensus. This is supported by later scholars who note that the earlier ruling is based on a narration (riwaya) while the commentator's view is based on rational understanding (diraya). A further discussion from al-Fath clarifies that the certainty of the specification is not a specific item, so returning to the original (mut'ah or mahr al-mithl) is appropriate. The passage concludes with a reference to al-Nahr stating that the issue of marrying on a specific slave is sufficient to answer the difficulty.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower; an amount appropriate for a woman of her status, considering her family, beauty, intellect, and other relevant factors.
التحليف (al-tahlif): Administering an oath; requiring a party to swear regarding a disputed claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a wife claims a mahr of 1000 dirhams and the husband denies any named mahr, what is the ruling?
A) The wife must take an oath, and if she swears, she gets 1000 dirhams.
B) The husband must take an oath, and if he swears, mahr al-mithl is given; if he refuses, he pays 1000 dirhams.
C) Mahr al-mithl is given immediately without any oath.
D) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is disputed.

Key Takeaway
When the existence of a named mahr is disputed, mahr al-mithl is wajib by Hanafi consensus, but the crucial procedural question is whether the denying spouse must swear an oath—the later school prefers the oath requirement, making its outcome decisive.

Disagreement on the Existence of a Named Mahr
Commentary on intra-Hanafi dispute regarding oath in mahr disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on requiring an oath when spouses dispute the existence of a named mahr, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute a named mahr, the Sahibayn require an oath; Abu Hanifa does not — the cautious view prevails.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when one spouse claims a specific mahr was named and the other denies it? While all three imams agree that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib if no named mahr is proven, they differ on whether the denying spouse must take an oath. Understanding this difference is crucial for a mufti who must determine the proper procedure and the resulting obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon ruling
All Hanafi imams agree that if spouses dispute the existence of a named mahr, mahr al-mithl (proper dower) becomes wajib. This is the starting point.
The agreement is on the outcome, not the procedural steps.
2
Note the procedural difference on oaths
Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is administered in marriage matters, so mahr al-mithl is wajib immediately. The Sahibayn require the denier to take an oath; if he refuses, the named mahr is confirmed, if he swears, mahr al-mithl is wajib.
This difference stems from viewing mahr as either a pure marriage matter (Abu Hanifa) or a financial right (Sahibayn).
3
Understand the rationale for each position
Abu Hanifa argues that oaths are not taken in nikah because marriage is a sacred contract. The Sahibayn counter that mahr is a financial obligation, and oaths are used to resolve financial claims.
The Sahibayn's view is considered more cautious (ihtiyat) and is preferred in practice.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities like Sadr al-Shari'ah support the Sahibayn's requirement of an oath. This is now the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on caution and practical utility.

قوله : (ولو) في أصل المسمى يجب مهر المثل أي ولو اختلفا في أصل المسمى بأن ادعاه أحدهما ونفاه الآخر فإنه يجب مهر المثل اتفاقاً والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الدخول اتفاقاً، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن أحدهما يدعي التسمية والآخر ينكره فالقول قول المنكر، وكذا عند أبي يوسف لتعذر القضاء بالمسمى بخلاف ما تقدم لأنه أمكن القضاء بالمتفق وهو الأقل ما لم يكن مستنكراً. وقوله في الهداية «لأن مهر المثل هو الأصل عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد مشكل لأنه قدم قبله أن المسمى هو الأصل عند محمد وإنما مهر المثل هو الأصل عند الإمام فقط . كذا ذكره الشارحون . وجوابه أنه الأصل في التحكيم عندهما كما . في الاختلاف في القدر وليس مراده الاصالة بالنسبة إلى المسمى فلا إشكال أطلقه فشمل الاختلاف في حياتهما وبعد موت أحدهما سواء كان في الأصل أو في القدر، فحكم الاختلاف بعد موت أحدهما في القدر كهو في حياتهما كما في المحيط ، وأما في الأصل فقال في التبيين ولو كان الاختلاف بعد موت أحدهما فالجواب فيه كالجواب في حياتهما بالاتفاق لأن اعتبار مهر المثل لا يسقط بموت أحدهما وكذا لو طلقها قبل الدخول اهـ. يعني تحكم المتعة. وفي البزازية ادعت المسمى بعد موته فأقر الوارث به لكن قال لا أعرف قدره حبس، وظاهر كلام المصنف أنه يجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وليس كذلك، بل لا يزاد على ما ادعته المرأة لو كانت هي المدعية للتسمية ولا ينقص عما ادعاه الزوج لو كان هو المدعى لها كما أشار إليه في البدائع، ولم يتعرض الشارحون للتحليف. وذكر صدر الشريعة أنه يحلف عندهما، فإن نكل ثبت المسمى، وإن حلف المنكر وجب مهر المثل، وأما عند أبي حنيفة ينبغي أن لا يحلف المنكر لأنه لا تحليف عنده في النكاح فيجب مهر المثل اهـ. وفيه نظر
His statement: 'And if [they differ] concerning the foundation of the named [dower]', mahr al-mithl is obligatory, meaning even if they differ concerning the foundation of the named dower, such that one claims it and the other denies it, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory by agreement, and the mut'ah [is obligatory] if he divorces her before consummation by agreement. As for according to them two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], it is apparent because one claims a naming and the other denies it, so the word is the word of the denier. Likewise according to Abu Yusuf, due to the inability to adjudicate the named [dower], contrary to what preceded because it was possible to adjudicate the agreed-upon [amount], which is the least, unless it is disapproved. And his statement in al-Hidayah: 'Because mahr al-mithl is the original according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is problematic because he stated before that the named is the original according to Muhammad, and mahr al-mithl is only the original according to the Imam alone.' Thus mentioned the commentators. And its answer: it is the original in arbitration (tahkim) according to them, as in the disagreement concerning the amount, and his intent is not originality in relation to the named, so no problem. He made it general so it includes the disagreement during their lifetimes and after the death of one of them, whether concerning the foundation or the amount. So the ruling of disagreement after the death of one of them concerning the amount is like it is during their lifetimes, as in al-Muhit. As for the foundation, it was said in al-Tabyin: 'And if the disagreement is after the death of one of them, then the answer in it is like the answer during their lifetimes by agreement, because consideration of mahr al-mithl is not abrogated by the death of one of them.' Likewise if he divorced her before consummation, end. Meaning he rules for mut'ah. And in al-Bazzaziyya: She claimed the named [dower] after his death, and the heir acknowledged it but said I do not know its amount, he is imprisoned. And the apparent statement of the author is that mahr al-mithl is obligatory whatever it may be, but it is not so. Rather, it is not increased beyond what the woman claimed if she is the claimant of the naming, nor decreased from what the husband claimed if he is the claimant for her, as indicated in al-Bada'i'. And the commentators did not address the oath. And Sadr al-Shari'ah mentioned that he takes an oath according to them [the two companions], and if he refuses, the named is established, and if the denier takes an oath, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. As for according to Abu Hanifa, it is appropriate that the denier should not take an oath because there is no oath-taking in marriage according to him, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. End. And in it is a consideration.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding a dispute between spouses about whether a specific mahr (dower) was named or not. The base ruling is that if they differ on the existence of a named mahr, then mahr al-mithl (proper dower) is obligatory by agreement among the Hanafi imams. If the husband divorced her before consummation, then mut'ah (consolatory gift) is obligatory instead. The commentator then addresses an apparent contradiction from al-Hidayah: it states that mahr al-mithl is the original according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but earlier it said the named is original for Muhammad. The answer is that 'original' here means in arbitration (tahkim), i.e., when the spouses disagree and no named amount can be confirmed, the default is mahr al-mithl. For Muhammad, the named mahr is the original when it is agreed upon, but when disputed, arbitration falls back to mahr al-mithl. The ruling applies whether the disagreement is during lifetime or after the death of one spouse. The commentator also clarifies that the author's sweeping statement that mahr al-mithl is wajib regardless of amount is not absolute; the claimed amounts by either party act as limits. Regarding oaths, Sadr al-Shari'ah explains that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the denier of the named mahr takes an oath; if he refuses, the named is confirmed. According to Abu Hanifa, no oath is taken in marriage matters, so mahr al-mithl is immediately wajib. The phrase 'in it is a consideration' signals a point of debate among later scholars.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to that of women of similar status to the wife, determined when no specific dower is named or agreed upon.
أصل المسمى (asl al-musamma): The foundation or existence of a specifically named dower as agreed upon by the spouses.
تحليف (tahlif): Administering an oath to a party in a dispute to ascertain the truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what happens if the denier of a named mahr refuses to take an oath?
A) Mahr al-mithl is wajib immediately.
B) The named mahr is confirmed and becomes due.
C) The case is dismissed.
D) The wife must provide evidence.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over the existence of a named mahr, the Hanafi mufta bihi position requires the denying spouse to take an oath; refusal establishes the named mahr, while swearing results in mahr al-mithl.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Dispute over Mahr After Both Spouses Die: Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr after death of both spouses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on mahr disputes after both spouses die, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
After both die, Abu Hanifa always favours the husband's heirs; the fatwa follows the students' nuanced view.

When both spouses die and their heirs disagree about the mahr—whether it was named or its amount—the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. The matn states a general rule, but the commentary reveals a three-way split between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students. This lesson unpacks those positions, their reasoning, and which one prevails for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Both spouses have died, and their heirs differ about the mahr. There are two types of dispute: over the amount (qadr) of a named mahr, or over the very existence (asl) of a named mahr (i.e., whether any mahr was agreed upon at all).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the word (al-qawl) is given to the husband's heirs in both types of dispute. If the dispute is over the amount, what the husband's heirs acknowledge is binding. If over the existence, nothing is owed because they deny a named mahr.
His reasoning: the mahr is a debt on the husband, and after death, the burden of proof falls on the claimants (wife's heirs).
3
State the students' (Sahibayn) positions
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad treat the dispute after death like a dispute during life. Muhammad says: in both amount and origin disputes, if the marriage is apparent (zahir), mahr al-mithl is adjudged. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: in amount disputes, the word is with the husband's heirs; in origin disputes, mahr al-mithl is adjudged unless the husband's heirs prove payment or acknowledgment.
They view the mahr as a debt that does not automatically fall due to death.
4
Identify the reasoning behind the dispute
The commentary mentions a talil (reasoning) for Abu Hanifa's position: mahr al-mithl resembles both the named mahr (which does not fall with one death) and maintenance (which falls with death). Because of this dual resemblance, it falls with the death of both. However, the text from Abu Hanifa contradicts this, and later scholars (like in Fath al-Qadir) note the weakness of that reasoning.
The actual reasoning for Abu Hanifa is based on the extinction of the wife's peers (aqran) after long time, making it impossible to determine mahr al-mithl.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to Fatawa Qadikhan, the fatwa is on the statement of the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The practical outcome: if both die and the marriage is apparent, mahr al-mithl is due unless the husband's heirs bring evidence of payment or acknowledgment. Also, an exception is noted if the woman had surrendered herself (taslim), indicating she must have received something, so mahr al-mithl is not adjudged.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of tarjih (preference) among conflicting opinions.

القدر فالقول لورثته ومن بعث إلى امرأته شيئاً فقالت هو هدية وقال هو من المهر عنه، لظهوره. وفي جامع الفصولين ادعت مهرها بعد موته فادعى الوارث الخلع قبل الموت بعد إنكار أصل النكاح لا تسمع، وإن ادعى الإبراء ففيها أقوال ثالثها إن ادعى الإبراء عن المهر لا تسمع وإن ادعى الإبراء عن دعوى المهر تسمع اهـ . قوله : (ولو مانا ولو في القدر فالقول لورثته أي لو مات الزوجان واختلف ورثتهما فالقول لورثة الزوج، سواء كان في القدر أو في الأصل، فإن كان في القدر لزم ما اعترفوا به، وإن كان في الأصل بأن أدعى ورثتها المسمى وأنكره ورثته فلا شيء عليهم. وهذا عند الإمام، عندهما الاختلاف بعد موتهما كالاختلاف في حياتهما، فإن اختلفا في القدر قال محمد: يقضى بمهر المثل. وقال أبو يوسف : القول لورثة الزوج، وإن اختلفا في الأصل يقضى بمهر المثل إذا كان النكاح ظاهراً إلا إذا أقامت ورثته البينة على إيفاء المهر أو على إقرارها به أو إقرار ورثتها به لأنه كان ديناً في ذمته فلا يسقط بالموت كالمسمى، فإن علم أنها ماتت أولاً سقط نصيبه منه وما بقي فلورثتها . وله أن موتهما يدل على انقراض أقرانها فبمهر من يقدر القاضي مهر المثل. كذا في الهداية. وهذا يدل على أن المسألة مصورة في التقادم، فلو كان العهد قريباً قضى به وعلى أنه لو أقيمت البينة على المهر قضى بها على ورثة الزوج صرح بالثاني في المحيط وشرح الطحاوي وعبارة المحيط قال أبو حنيفة : لا أقضي بشيء حتى يثبت بالبينة أصل التسمية. وبهذا اندفع ما علل به بعض المشايخ له من أن المثل من حيث هو قيمة البضع يشبه المسمى، ومن حيث إنه يجب بغير شرط يشبه النفقة والصلة، فباعتبار الشبه الأول لم يسقط بموت أحدهما وباعتبار الشبه الثاني يسقط فسقط بموتهما فإنه يقتضي أنه لا تسمع البينة عليه بعد موتهما لسقوطه أصلاً، والمنصوص عن الإمام خلافه كما علمت ولذا قال في فتح القدير: إن تعليل الهداية أو جه، وفي فتاوى قاضيخان الفتوى على قولهما وفي المحيط قال مشايخنا : هذا كله إذا لم تسلم المرأة نفسها، فإن سلمت نفسها ثم وقع الإختلاف في حيال الحياة أو بعد الممات فإنه لا يحكم بمهر المثل لأنا نعلم أن المرأة لا تسلم نفسها من غير أن تتعجل من مهرها شيئاً عادة فيقال لها لا بد أن تقري بما تعجلت وإلا قضينا عليك بالمتعارف، ثم يعمل في الباقي كما ذكرنا اهـ. وأقره عليه الشارحون، ولا يخفى أن محله فيما إذا ادعى الزوج إيصال شيء إليها، أما لو لم يدع فلا ذلك. وفي المحيط معزياً إلى النوادر وامرأة ادعت على زوجها بعد موته أن لها عليه ألف درهم من مهرها فالقول قولها إلى تمام مهر مثلها عند أبي حنيفة لأن مهر المثل يشهد لها اهـ. وهذا يخالف ما ذكره المشايخ سابقاً. وفي الخلاصة من الفصل الثاني عشر من كتاب الدعوى : امرأة ادعت على وارث زوجها مهرها فأنكر الوارث يوقف قدر مهر مثلها ويقول له القاضي أكان مهر مثلها كذا أعلى ذلك؟ إن قالوا لا قال : أكان كذا دون ما قال في المرة من الأولى إلى أن ينتهي إلى مقدار مهر مثلها اهـ.
The statement: the word is for his heirs. And from the chapter: If someone sends something to his wife and she says it is a gift and he says it is from the mahr, the word is his due to its apparent nature. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: A woman claims her mahr after his death, and the heir claims khul' before death after denying the original marriage: it is not heard. And if he claims discharge, there are sayings, the third: if he claims discharge from the mahr it is not heard, but if he claims discharge from the claim of mahr it is heard. End. His statement: (And if they die, even in the amount, the word is for his heirs) i.e., if both spouses die and their heirs differ, the word is for the husband's heirs, whether in amount or in origin. If it is in the amount, what they acknowledge is binding; if in origin, by the wife's heirs claiming the named [mahr] and his heirs denying it, nothing is on them. This is according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. According to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], the dispute after their death is like the dispute during their lives. If they differ in amount, Muhammad said: it is adjudged with mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf said: the word is for the husband's heirs. And if they differ in origin, it is adjudged with mahr al-mithl if the marriage is apparent, unless his heirs establish evidence of payment of the mahr or of her acknowledgment of it or of her heirs' acknowledgment, because it was a debt in his liability, so it does not fall due to death like the named [mahr]. If it is known that she died first, his share of it falls and what remains is for her heirs. And for him: their death indicates the extinction of her peers, so by whose mahr does the judge determine mahr al-mithl? Thus in al-Hidayah. And this indicates that the issue is portrayed in remote time; if the time was recent, it would be judged accordingly. And also that if evidence of the mahr is established, it is judged against the husband's heirs; explicit about the second in al-Muhit and Sharh al-Tahawi. The wording of al-Muhit: Abu Hanifa said: I do not judge anything until the origin of the naming is confirmed by evidence. And by this is refuted what some teachers reasoned for him: that the mithl, in that it is the value of the vulva, resembles the named mahr, and in that it is obligatory without condition, resembles maintenance and gifts. By consideration of the first resemblance it does not fall due to the death of one of them, and by the second resemblance it falls, so it falls by the death of both, which implies that evidence is not heard after their death because it falls completely, while the text from the Imam is contrary as you know. Therefore it was said in Fath al-Qadir: the reasoning of al-Hidayah is weak. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: the fatwa is on their statement. And in al-Muhit: our teachers said: all this if the woman did not surrender herself. If she surrendered herself then the dispute occurs during life or after death, then mahr al-mithl is not adjudged, because we know that a woman does not surrender herself without having taken something of her mahr customarily. So it is said to her: you must acknowledge what you took, otherwise we judge against you with the customary. Then action is taken on the remainder as we mentioned. And the commentators agreed with him. It is not hidden that its place is when the husband claims delivering something to her; if he does not claim, then not. And in al-Muhit, attributed to al-Nawadir: a woman claimed against her husband after his death that he owed her a thousand dirhams of her mahr; the word is hers up to her full mahr al-mithl according to Abu Hanifa because mahr al-mithl testifies for her. This contradicts what the teachers mentioned previously. And in al-Khulasah from the twelfth chapter of the book of claims: a woman claimed her mahr from her husband's heir; the heir denied; the amount of her mahr al-mithl is suspended, and the judge says to him: was her mahr al-mithl like this? Higher than that? If they say no, he says: was it lower than what he said in the first instance until reaching the amount of her mahr al-mithl.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage discusses the dispute among Hanafi imams when both spouses die and their heirs disagree about the mahr. The matn states that if the spouses die and there is a dispute over the amount (qadr) or the very existence (asl) of the mahr, the word is given to the husband's heirs. The commentary by al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on this, noting that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the word is with the husband's heirs whether the dispute is over the amount or the origin. If the dispute is over the amount, the heirs' acknowledgment is binding; if over the origin (i.e., the wife's heirs claim that a mahr was named while the husband's heirs deny any named mahr), then nothing is owed. However, the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) treat the dispute after death like a dispute during life. If the dispute is over the amount, Muhammad says mahr al-mithl is adjudged, while Abu Yusuf says the word is with the husband's heirs. If the dispute is over the origin, mahr al-mithl is adjudged if the marriage is apparent (zahir), unless the husband's heirs bring evidence of payment or acknowledgment. The passage then delves into the rationale: some teachers reasoned that mahr al-mithl falls due to the death of both because it resembles both the named mahr (which does not fall) and maintenance (which falls), so it falls when both die. But the text from Abu Hanifa contradicts this. Later, the passage cites an exception: if the woman had surrendered herself (taslim) before the dispute, then mahr al-mithl is not adjudged because custom indicates she must have taken something. The fatwa according to Qadikhan is on the statement of the two students. Finally, a contradictory narration from al-Nawadir is mentioned where the woman's word is taken up to mahr al-mithl after the husband's death, but the author notes this conflicts with earlier statements. The discussion shows the complexity of Hanafi inheritance and mahr disputes.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr due when no specific mahr is named, determined by the value of the woman's peers.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The act of specifying a mahr amount in the marriage contract.
قدر (qadr): The specific amount of mahr that was named or claimed.
أصل (asl): The very existence of a named mahr (i.e., whether a mahr was agreed upon at all).
ورثة (waratha): Heirs; in this context, the heirs of the deceased spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, what is the outcome when both spouses die and their heirs dispute the existence of a named mahr (asl)?
A) The husband's heirs' word is accepted, so nothing is owed.
B) The wife's heirs' word is accepted, so the claimed amount is paid.
C) Mahr al-mithl is adjudged if the marriage is apparent.
D) The judge divides the claimed amount equally.

Key Takeaway
After both spouses die, the Hanafi mufta bihi rule is that if the marriage is apparent, mahr al-mithl is due for disputes over the existence or amount of the mahr, unless the husband's heirs prove it was paid or acknowledged.

Husband Sends Something to Wife: Gift or Part of Mahr?
Determines whose word is taken in mahr/gift disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi evidentiary rule for disputes over items sent by a husband to his wife, distinguishing between perishable food (wife's word) and other items (husband's word).

Core Idea
Custom decides: husband's word for non-food, wife's word for perishable gifts.

When a husband sends something to his wife and they later disagree whether it was a gift or part of the mahr, who is believed? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq provides a clear Hanafi rule based on custom (urf) and the nature of the item. The key distinction is whether the item is 'prepared for eating' (perishable food) – in which case custom presumes it is a gift and the wife's word is taken – or not, in which case the husband's word prevails. This ruling illustrates how Hanafi fiqh uses custom to resolve evidentiary conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The husband sends an item to his wife. She claims it is a gift (hadiyah); he claims it is part of the mahr. Whose word is accepted?
This is a typical marital financial dispute.
2
State the general rule
For items not 'prepared for eating' (ghayr muhayya' li'l-akl), the husband's word is taken. The reasoning: he is the owner, knows his intention, and the custom suggests he seeks to fulfill his obligation.
The husband is the owner and the one providing.
3
Define 'prepared for eating'
Al-Walwaliji defines it as what does not remain and spoils, e.g., fresh dates, flour, honey. These are customarily given as gifts.
The definition is based on perishability and custom.
4
Apply the exception
For such perishable food items, the wife's word is taken because custom contradicts the husband's claim – the apparent suggests a gift.
Custom overrides the default rule.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi nuance
Abu al-Layth broadens the analysis: for items not obligatory on the husband, his word; for obligatory items (like basic clothing), her word. The mufta bihi aligns with this broader view.
This shows how later scholars refined the rule.
